\xc3\x96rlygsson</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Legislature</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Althing" title="Althing">Althing</a></td></tr><tr </div></th><td>\n930\xe2\x80\x931262</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">\xe2\x80\xa2&#160;<span class="nowrap"><a class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cia.gov/library/publications/the-world-factbook/fields/2172.html#Govt">"CIA&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 The World Factbook&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 Field Listing&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 Distribution of family income&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 Gini index"</a>. United States government<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">14 September</span> 2008</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=CIA+%E2%80%93+The+World+Factbook+%E2%80%93+Field+Listing+%E2%80%93+Distribution+of+family+income+%E2%80%93+Gini+index&amp;rft.pub=United+States+government&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.cia.gov%2Flibrary%2Fpublications%2Fthe-world-factbook%2Ffields%2F2172.html%23Govt&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AIceland" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Iceland</b> (<a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a>: <i lang="is">\xc3\x8dsland</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Icelandic" title="Help:IPA/Icelandic">[\xcb\x88istlant]</a></span>)<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic</a> <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> in the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Ocean" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic</a>, with a population of 348,580 and an area of 103,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (40,000&#160;sq&#160;mi), making it the most sparsely populated country in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Statice_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statice-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjav\xc3\xadk">Reykjav\xc3\xadk</a>. Reykjav\xc3\xadk and the surrounding areas in the southwest of the country are home to over two-thirds of the population.\n</p><p>Iceland is <a href="/wiki/High_island" title="High island">volcanically</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_(geology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Geothermal (geology)">geologically active</a>. The interior consists of a plateau characterised by sand and <a href="/wiki/Lava_field" title="Lava field">lava fields</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountains">mountains</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">glaciers</a>, and many <a href="/wiki/River" title="River">glacial rivers</a> flow to the sea through the lowlands. Iceland is warmed by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a> and has a temperate climate, despite a high latitude just outside the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Circle" title="Arctic Circle">Arctic Circle</a>. Its high latitude and marine influence keep summers chilly, with most of the archipelago having a <a href="/wiki/Tundra_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Tundra climate">tundra climate</a>.\n</p><p>According to the ancient manuscript <i><a href="/wiki/Landn%C3%A1mab%C3%B3k" title="Landn\xc3\xa1mab\xc3\xb3k">Landn\xc3\xa1mab\xc3\xb3k</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Settlement_of_Iceland" title="Settlement of Iceland">settlement of Iceland</a> began in 874 AD when the <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norwegian</a> chieftain <a href="/wiki/Ing%C3%B3lfr_Arnarson" title="Ing\xc3\xb3lfr Arnarson">Ing\xc3\xb3lfr Arnarson</a> became the first permanent settler on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-tomasson_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tomasson-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In the following centuries, <a href="/wiki/Norwegians" title="Norwegians">Norwegians</a>, and to a lesser extent other <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavians</a>, emigrated to Iceland, bringing with them <a href="/wiki/Thrall" title="Thrall">thralls</a> (i.e., slaves or serfs) of <a href="/wiki/Gaels" title="Gaels">Gaelic</a> origin. The island was governed as an <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_Commonwealth" title="Icelandic Commonwealth">independent commonwealth</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Althing" title="Althing">Althing</a>, one of the world\'s oldest functioning legislative assemblies. Following a <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Sturlungs" class="mw-redirect" title="Age of Sturlungs">period of civil strife</a>, Iceland acceded to Norwegian rule in the 13th century. The establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Kalmar_Union" title="Kalmar Union">Kalmar Union</a> in 1397 united the kingdoms of Norway, Denmark, and Sweden. Iceland thus followed Norway\'s integration to that union and came under Danish rule, after Sweden\'s secession from that union in 1523. Although the Danish kingdom introduced <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> forcefully in 1550, Iceland remained a distant semi-colonial territory in which Danish institutions and infrastructures were conspicuous by their absence. In the wake of the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, Iceland\'s struggle for independence took form and culminated in <a href="/wiki/Danish%E2%80%93Icelandic_Act_of_Union" title="Danish\xe2\x80\x93Icelandic Act of Union">independence in 1918</a> and the founding of a <a href="/wiki/Founding_of_the_Republic_of_Iceland" class="mw-redirect" title="Founding of the Republic of Iceland">republic in 1944</a>. Until the 20th century, Iceland relied largely on subsistence fishing and agriculture, and was among the poorest countries in Europe. Industrialisation of the fisheries and <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a> aid following <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> brought prosperity, and Iceland became one of the wealthiest and most developed nations in the world. In 1994, it became a part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a>, which further diversified the economy into sectors such as finance, biotechnology, and manufacturing.\n</p><p>Iceland has a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a> with relatively low taxes, compared to other <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a> countries.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> It maintains a <a href="/wiki/Nordic_model" title="Nordic model">Nordic social welfare system</a> that provides <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a> and tertiary education for its citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Iceland ranks high in economic, political, and social stability and equality. In 2016, it was ranked as the ninth most developed country in the world by the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">United Nations\' Human Development Index</a>, and it ranks first on the <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">Global Peace Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HDI_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDI-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Iceland runs almost completely on <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a>. Affected by the ongoing <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x932008">worldwide financial crisis</a>, the nation\'s entire banking system <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%932011_Icelandic_financial_crisis" title="2008\xe2\x80\x932011 Icelandic financial crisis">systemically failed</a> in October 2008, leading to a <a href="/wiki/Depression_(economics)" title="Depression (economics)">severe depression</a>, substantial <a href="/wiki/2009_Icelandic_financial_crisis_protests" title="2009 Icelandic financial crisis protests">political unrest</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Icesave_dispute" title="Icesave dispute">Icesave dispute</a>, and the institution of <a href="/wiki/Capital_control" title="Capital control">capital controls</a>. Some bankers were jailed.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Since then, the economy has made a significant recovery, in large part due to a surge in <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Iceland" title="Tourism in Iceland">tourism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Iceland" title="Culture of Iceland">Icelandic culture</a> is founded upon the nation\'s Scandinavian heritage. Most Icelanders are descendants of <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gael" class="mw-redirect" title="Gael">Gaelic</a> settlers. <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a>, a <a href="/wiki/North_Germanic_languages" title="North Germanic languages">North Germanic language</a>, is descended from <a href="/wiki/Old_West_Norse" class="mw-redirect" title="Old West Norse">Old West Norse</a> and is closely related to <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_dialects" title="Norwegian dialects">West Norwegian dialects</a>. The country\'s cultural heritage includes traditional <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_cuisine" title="Icelandic cuisine">Icelandic cuisine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_literature" title="Icelandic literature">Icelandic literature</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sagas_of_Icelanders" title="Sagas of Icelanders">medieval sagas</a>. Iceland has the smallest population of any <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_NATO" title="Member states of NATO">NATO member</a> and is the only one with <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_without_armed_forces" title="List of countries without armed forces">no standing army</a>, with a lightly armed <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_Coast_Guard" title="Icelandic Coast Guard">coast guard</a> in charge of defence.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Iceland" title="Names of Iceland">Names of Iceland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Norsemen_Landing_in_Iceland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Norsemen_Landing_in_Iceland.jpg/220px-Norsemen_Landing_in_Iceland.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Norsemen_Landing_in_Iceland.jpg/330px-Norsemen_Landing_in_Iceland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Norsemen_Landing_in_Iceland.jpg/440px-Norsemen_Landing_in_Iceland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2768" data-file-height="1887" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Norsemen_Landing_in_Iceland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Norsemen landing in Iceland \xe2\x80\x93 a 19th-century depiction by <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Wergeland" title="Oscar Wergeland">Oscar Wergeland</a>.</div></div></div><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sagas_of_Icelanders" title="Sagas of Icelanders">Sagas of Icelanders</a> say that a Norwegian named <a href="/wiki/Naddodd" title="Naddodd">Naddodd</a> (or Naddador) was the first <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norseman</a> to reach Iceland, and in the 9th century he named it Sn\xc3\xa6land or "snow land" because it was snowing. Following Naddodd, the Swede <a href="/wiki/Gar%C3%B0ar_Svavarsson" title="Gar\xc3\xb0ar Svavarsson">Gar\xc3\xb0ar Svavarsson</a> arrived, and so the island was then called Gar\xc3\xb0arsh\xc3\xb3lmur which means "Gar\xc3\xb0ar\xe2\x80\x99s Isle".\n</p><p>Then came a Viking named <a href="/wiki/Fl%C3%B3ki_Vilger%C3%B0arson" class="mw-redirect" title="Fl\xc3\xb3ki Vilger\xc3\xb0arson">Fl\xc3\xb3ki Vilger\xc3\xb0arson</a>; his daughter drowned en route, then his livestock starved to death. The sagas say that the rather despondent Fl\xc3\xb3ki climbed a mountain and saw a fjord (<a href="/wiki/Arnarfj%C3%B6r%C3%B0ur" title="Arnarfj\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb0ur">Arnarfj\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb0ur</a>) full of icebergs, which led him to give the island its new and present name.<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The notion that Iceland\xe2\x80\x99s Viking settlers chose that name to discourage oversettlement of their verdant isle is a myth.<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iceland" title="History of Iceland">History of Iceland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Icelandic_history" title="Timeline of Icelandic history">Timeline of Icelandic history</a></div>\n<div style="float:left;border:1px solid rgb(170, 170, 170);width:100%"><div style="text-align:left; padding:1em; font-size:95%; margin:1em; style="margin-left:93.531468531469%; margin-top:0; position:relative"><span style="position:relative; top:0.25em; left:-1.5px">&#160;</span><span style="font-size:smaller; position:relative; line-height:3px; overflow:visible;left:0em; top:0em; z-index:997">1944</span></div></div></div></div></div><div style="clear:left;"></div>\n<h3><span id="874.E2.80.931262:_Settlement_and_Commonwealth"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="874\xe2\x80\x931262:_Settlement_and_Commonwealth">874\xe2\x80\x931262: Settlement and Commonwealth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 874\xe2\x80\x931262: Settlement and Commonwealth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Settlement_of_Iceland" title="Settlement of Iceland">Settlement of Iceland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_Commonwealth" title="Icelandic Commonwealth">Icelandic Commonwealth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christianisation_of_Iceland" class="mw-redirect" title="Christianisation of Iceland">Christianisation of Iceland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ingolf_by_Raadsig.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Ingolf_by_Raadsig.jpg/220px-Ingolf_by_Raadsig.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Ingolf_by_Raadsig.jpg/330px-Ingolf_by_Raadsig.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Ingolf_by_Raadsig.jpg/440px-Ingolf_by_Raadsig.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1568" data-file-height="1244" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ingolf_by_Raadsig.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ing%C3%B3lfr_Arnarson" title="Ing\xc3\xb3lfr Arnarson">Ing\xc3\xb3lfr Arnarson</a> (modern Icelandic: <i>Ing\xc3\xb3lfur Arnarson</i>), the first permanent Scandinavian settler</div></div></div>\n<p>According to both <a href="/wiki/Landn%C3%A1mab%C3%B3k" title="Landn\xc3\xa1mab\xc3\xb3k">Landn\xc3\xa1mab\xc3\xb3k</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Dslendingab%C3%B3k" title="\xc3\x8dslendingab\xc3\xb3k">\xc3\x8dslendingab\xc3\xb3k</a>, monks known as the <a href="/wiki/Papar" title="Papar">Papar</a> lived in Iceland before Scandinavian settlers arrived, possibly members of a <a href="/wiki/Hiberno-Scottish_mission" title="Hiberno-Scottish mission">Hiberno-Scottish mission</a>. Recent <a href="/wiki/Archaeological" class="mw-redirect" title="Archaeological">archaeological</a> excavations have revealed the ruins of a cabin in <a href="/wiki/Hafnir" title="Hafnir">Hafnir</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Reykjanes" title="Reykjanes">Reykjanes peninsula</a>. <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dating" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon dating">Carbon dating</a> indicates that it was abandoned sometime between 770 and 880.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, archeologists uncovered a <a href="/wiki/Longhouse" title="Longhouse">longhouse</a> in <a href="/wiki/St%C3%B6%C3%B0varfj%C3%B6r%C3%B0ur" title="St\xc3\xb6\xc3\xb0varfj\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb0ur">St\xc3\xb6\xc3\xb0varfj\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb0ur</a> that has been dated to as early as 800.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Swedish Viking explorer <a href="/wiki/Gar%C3%B0ar_Svavarsson" title="Gar\xc3\xb0ar Svavarsson">Gar\xc3\xb0ar Svavarsson</a> was the first to circumnavigate Iceland in 870 and establish that it was an island.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> He stayed over winter and built a house in <a href="/wiki/H%C3%BAsav%C3%ADk" title="H\xc3\xbasav\xc3\xadk">H\xc3\xbasav\xc3\xadk</a>. Gar\xc3\xb0ar departed the following summer but one of his men, <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A1ttfari" title="N\xc3\xa1ttfari">N\xc3\xa1ttfari</a>, decided to stay behind with two slaves. N\xc3\xa1ttfari settled in what is now known as N\xc3\xa1ttfarav\xc3\xadk and he and his slaves became the first permanent residents of Iceland.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Norwegian-Norse chieftain <a href="/wiki/Ing%C3%B3lfr_Arnarson" title="Ing\xc3\xb3lfr Arnarson">Ing\xc3\xb3lfr Arnarson</a> built his homestead in present-day Reykjav\xc3\xadk in 874. Ing\xc3\xb3lfr was followed by many other emigrant settlers, largely Scandinavians and their <a href="/wiki/Thrall" title="Thrall">thralls</a>, many of whom were Irish or Scottish.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> By 930, most <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable land</a> on the island had been claimed; the <a href="/wiki/Althing" title="Althing">Althing</a>, a legislative and judicial assembly, was initiated to regulate the Icelandic Commonwealth. Lack of arable land also served as an impetus to the <a href="/wiki/Norse_colonization_of_Greenland" class="mw-redirect" title="Norse colonization of Greenland">settlement of Greenland</a> starting in 986.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The period of these early settlements coincided with the <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Warm_Period" title="Medieval Warm Period">Medieval Warm Period</a>, when temperatures were similar to those of the early 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> At this time, about 25% of Iceland was covered with forest, compared to 1% in the present day.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Christianity was adopted <a href="/wiki/Christianisation_of_Iceland" class="mw-redirect" title="Christianisation of Iceland">by consensus</a> around 999\xe2\x80\x931000, although <a href="/wiki/Norse_paganism" class="mw-redirect" title="Norse paganism">Norse paganism</a> persisted among some segments of the population for some years afterwards.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Middle_Ages">The Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Age_of_the_Sturlungs" title="Age of the Sturlungs">Age of the Sturlungs</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bolungarvik_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Bolungarvik_02.jpg/220px-Bolungarvik_02.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Bolungarvik_02.jpg/330px-Bolungarvik_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Bolungarvik_02.jpg/440px-Bolungarvik_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bolungarvik_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>\xc3\x93sv\xc3\xb6r</i>, a replica of an old fishing outpost outside <a href="/wiki/Bolungarv%C3%ADk" title="Bolungarv\xc3\xadk">Bolungarv\xc3\xadk</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_Commonwealth" title="Icelandic Commonwealth">Icelandic Commonwealth</a> lasted until the 13th century, when the political system devised by the original settlers proved unable to cope with the increasing power of Icelandic chieftains.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The internal struggles and civil strife of the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_the_Sturlungs" title="Age of the Sturlungs">Age of the Sturlungs</a> led to the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Old_Covenant_(Iceland)" title="Old Covenant (Iceland)">Old Covenant</a> in 1262, which ended the Commonwealth and brought Iceland under the Norwegian crown. Possession of Iceland passed from the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Norway_(872%E2%80%931397)" title="Kingdom of Norway (872\xe2\x80\x931397)">Kingdom of Norway (872\xe2\x80\x931397)</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Kalmar_Union" title="Kalmar Union">Kalmar Union</a> in 1415, when the kingdoms of Norway, Denmark and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> were united. After the break-up of the union in 1523, it remained a Norwegian dependency, as a part of <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Norway" title="Denmark\xe2\x80\x93Norway">Denmark\xe2\x80\x93Norway</a>.\n</p><p>In the ensuing centuries, Iceland became one of the poorest countries in Europe. Infertile soil, volcanic eruptions, deforestation and an unforgiving climate made for harsh life in a society where subsistence depended almost entirely on agriculture. The <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> swept Iceland twice, first in 1402\xe2\x80\x931404 and again in 1494\xe2\x80\x931495.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The former outbreak killed 50% to 60% of the population, and the latter 30% to 50%.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reformation_and_the_Early_Modern_period">Reformation and the Early Modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Reformation and the Early Modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_Reformation" title="Icelandic Reformation">Icelandic Reformation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danish-Icelandic_Trade_Monopoly" class="mw-redirect" title="Danish-Icelandic Trade Monopoly">Danish-Icelandic Trade Monopoly</a>, and <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B3%C3%B0uhar%C3%B0indin" class="mw-redirect" title="M\xc3\xb3\xc3\xb0uhar\xc3\xb0indin">M\xc3\xb3\xc3\xb0uhar\xc3\xb0indin</a></div>\n<p>Around the middle of the 16th century, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a>, King <a href="/wiki/Christian_III_of_Denmark" title="Christian III of Denmark">Christian III of Denmark</a> began to impose <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> on all his subjects. <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3n_Arason" title="J\xc3\xb3n Arason">J\xc3\xb3n Arason</a>, the last Catholic bishop of <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B3lar" title="H\xc3\xb3lar">H\xc3\xb3lar</a>, was beheaded in 1550 along with two of his sons. The country subsequently became officially Lutheran and Lutheranism has since remained the dominant religion.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gerardi_Mercatoris_Atlas,_sive,_Cosmographicae_Meditationes_de_Fabrica_Mundi_et_Fabricati_Figura_(24696368309).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Gerardi_Mercatoris_Atlas%2C_sive%2C_Cosmographicae_Meditationes_de_Fabrica_Mundi_et_Fabricati_Figura_%2824696368309%29.jpg/220px-Gerardi_Mercatoris_Atlas%2C_sive%2C_Cosmographicae_Meditationes_de_Fabrica_Mundi_et_Fabricati_Figura_%2824696368309%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Gerardi_Mercatoris_Atlas%2C_sive%2C_Cosmographicae_Meditationes_de_Fabrica_Mundi_et_Fabricati_Figura_%2824696368309%29.jpg/330px-Gerardi_Mercatoris_Atlas%2C_sive%2C_Cosmographicae_Meditationes_de_Fabrica_Mundi_et_Fabricati_Figura_%2824696368309%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Gerardi_Mercatoris_Atlas%2C_sive%2C_Cosmographicae_Meditationes_de_Fabrica_Mundi_et_Fabricati_Figura_%2824696368309%29.jpg/440px-Gerardi_Mercatoris_Atlas%2C_sive%2C_Cosmographicae_Meditationes_de_Fabrica_Mundi_et_Fabricati_Figura_%2824696368309%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1019" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gerardi_Mercatoris_Atlas,_sive,_Cosmographicae_Meditationes_de_Fabrica_Mundi_et_Fabricati_Figura_(24696368309).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of Iceland published in the early 17th century</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 17th and 18th centuries, Denmark imposed <a href="/wiki/Danish%E2%80%93Icelandic_Trade_Monopoly" title="Danish\xe2\x80\x93Icelandic Trade Monopoly">harsh trade restrictions</a> on Iceland. Natural disasters, including volcanic eruption and disease, contributed to a decreasing population. Pirates from several countries, including the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_Coast" title="Barbary Coast">Barbary Coast</a>, raided Iceland\'s coastal settlements and abducted people into slavery.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> A great <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> epidemic in the 18th century killed around a third of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In 1783 the <a href="/wiki/Laki" title="Laki">Laki</a> volcano erupted, with devastating effects.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In the years following the eruption, known as the <a href="/wiki/Mist_Hardships" class="mw-redirect" title="Mist Hardships">Mist Hardships</a> (Icelandic: <i>M\xc3\xb3\xc3\xb0uhar\xc3\xb0indin</i>), over half of all livestock in the country died. Around a quarter of the population starved to death in the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1814.E2.80.931918:_Independence_movement"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1814\xe2\x80\x931918:_Independence_movement">1814\xe2\x80\x931918: Independence movement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1814\xe2\x80\x931918: Independence movement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_independence_movement" title="Icelandic independence movement">Icelandic independence movement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fj%C3%B6lnir_(journal)" title="Fj\xc3\xb6lnir (journal)">Fj\xc3\xb6lnir (journal)</a></div>\n<p>In 1814, following the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, Denmark-Norway was broken up into two separate kingdoms via the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Kiel" title="Treaty of Kiel">Treaty of Kiel</a> but Iceland remained a Danish dependency. Throughout the 19th century, the country\'s climate continued to grow colder, resulting in mass emigration to the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>, particularly to the region of <a href="/wiki/Gimli,_Manitoba" title="Gimli, Manitoba">Gimli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">Manitoba</a> in Canada, which was sometimes referred to as <a href="/wiki/New_Iceland" title="New Iceland">New Iceland</a>. About 15,000 people emigrated, out of a total population of 70,000.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A national consciousness arose in the first half of the 19th century, inspired by <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">romantic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalist</a> ideas from mainland Europe. An Icelandic independence movement took shape in the 1850s under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3n_Sigur%C3%B0sson" title="J\xc3\xb3n Sigur\xc3\xb0sson">J\xc3\xb3n Sigur\xc3\xb0sson</a>, based on the burgeoning Icelandic nationalism inspired by the <i><a href="/wiki/Fj%C3%B6lnismenn" class="mw-redirect" title="Fj\xc3\xb6lnismenn">Fj\xc3\xb6lnismenn</a></i> and other Danish-educated Icelandic intellectuals. In 1874, Denmark granted Iceland a constitution and limited home rule. This was expanded in 1904, and <a href="/wiki/Hannes_Hafstein" title="Hannes Hafstein">Hannes Hafstein</a> served as the first <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Iceland" title="Minister for Iceland">Minister for Iceland</a> in the Danish cabinet.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1918.E2.80.931944:_Independence_and_the_Kingdom_of_Iceland"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1918\xe2\x80\x931944:_Independence_and_the_Kingdom_of_Iceland">1918\xe2\x80\x931944: Independence and the Kingdom of Iceland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1918\xe2\x80\x931944: Independence and the Kingdom of Iceland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iceland" title="Kingdom of Iceland">Kingdom of Iceland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Iceland" title="Invasion of Iceland">Invasion of Iceland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Iceland_in_World_War_II" title="Iceland in World War II">Iceland in World War II</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Berwick_(65).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/HMS_Berwick_%2865%29.jpg/220px-HMS_Berwick_%2865%29.jpg" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/HMS_Berwick_%2865%29.jpg/330px-HMS_Berwick_%2865%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/HMS_Berwick_%2865%29.jpg/440px-HMS_Berwick_%2865%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="784" data-file-height="598" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Berwick_(65).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/HMS_Berwick_(65)" title="HMS Berwick (65)">HMS&#160;<i>Berwick</i></a> led the British <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Iceland" title="Invasion of Iceland">invasion of Iceland</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Danish%E2%80%93Icelandic_Act_of_Union" title="Danish\xe2\x80\x93Icelandic Act of Union">Danish\xe2\x80\x93Icelandic Act of Union</a>, an agreement with Denmark signed on 1 December 1918 and valid for 25&#160;years, recognised Iceland as a fully sovereign and independent state in a <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> with Denmark. The Government of Iceland established an embassy in Copenhagen and requested that Denmark carry out on its behalf certain defence and foreign affairs matters, subject to consultation with the <a href="/wiki/Althing" title="Althing">Althing</a>. Danish embassies around the world displayed two coats of arms and two flags: those of the Kingdom of Denmark and those of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iceland" title="Kingdom of Iceland">Kingdom of Iceland</a>. Iceland\'s legal position became comparable to those of countries belonging to the Commonwealth of Nations such as Canada whose sovereign is Queen Elizabeth II.\n</p><p>During World War II, Iceland joined Denmark in asserting neutrality. After the <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Denmark" class="mw-redirect" title="German occupation of Denmark">German occupation of Denmark</a> on 9 April 1940, the Althing replaced the King with a regent and declared that the Icelandic government would take control of its own defence and foreign affairs. A month later, British armed forces <a href="/wiki/Operation_Fork" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Fork">invaded and occupied the country</a>, violating Icelandic <a href="/wiki/Neutrality_(international_relations)" class="mw-redirect" title="Neutrality (international relations)">neutrality</a>. In 1941, the Government of Iceland invited the United States to take over its defence so that Britain could use its troops elsewhere.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1944.E2.80.93present:_Republic_of_Iceland"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1944\xe2\x80\x93present:_Republic_of_Iceland">1944\xe2\x80\x93present: Republic of Iceland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1944\xe2\x80\x93present: Republic of Iceland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scylla-Odinn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Scylla-Odinn.jpg/220px-Scylla-Odinn.jpg" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Scylla-Odinn.jpg/330px-Scylla-Odinn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Scylla-Odinn.jpg/440px-Scylla-Odinn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="902" data-file-height="547" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scylla-Odinn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British and Icelandic vessels collide in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Cod_Wars" title="Cod Wars">Cod Wars</a> (Icelandic vessel is shown on the left; the British vessel is on the right)</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_constitutional_referendum,_1944" title="Icelandic constitutional referendum, 1944">Icelandic constitutional referendum, 1944</a>; <a href="/wiki/Iceland_in_the_Cold_War" title="Iceland in the Cold War">Iceland in the Cold War</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Cod_Wars" title="Cod Wars">Cod Wars</a></div>\n<p>On 31 December 1943, the <a href="/wiki/Danish%E2%80%93Icelandic_Act_of_Union" title="Danish\xe2\x80\x93Icelandic Act of Union">Danish\xe2\x80\x93Icelandic Act of Union</a> expired after 25&#160;years. Beginning on 20 May 1944, Icelanders voted in a four-day plebiscite on whether to terminate the personal union with Denmark, abolish the monarchy, and establish a republic. The vote was 97% to end the union, and 95% in favour of the new republican constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Iceland formally became a republic on 17 June 1944, with <a href="/wiki/Sveinn_Bj%C3%B6rnsson" title="Sveinn Bj\xc3\xb6rnsson">Sveinn Bj\xc3\xb6rnsson</a> as its first president.\n</p><p>In 1946, the US Defence Force Allied left Iceland. The nation formally became a member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> on 30 March 1949, amid <a href="/wiki/1949_anti-NATO_riot_in_Iceland" title="1949 anti-NATO riot in Iceland">domestic controversy and riots</a>. On 5 May 1951, a defence agreement was signed with the United States. American troops returned to Iceland as the <a href="/wiki/Iceland_Defence_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Iceland Defence Force">Iceland Defence Force</a>, and remained throughout the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. The US withdrew the last of its forces on 30 September 2006.\n</p><p>Iceland prospered during the Second World War. The immediate post-war period was followed by substantial <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">economic growth</a>, driven by industrialisation of the fishing industry and the US <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a> programme, through which Icelanders received the most aid per capita of any European country (at USD $209, with the war-ravaged <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> a distant second at USD $109).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 1970s were marked by the <a href="/wiki/Cod_Wars" title="Cod Wars">Cod Wars</a>\xe2\x80\x94several disputes with the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> over Iceland\'s extension of its fishing limits to 200&#160;nmi (370&#160;km) offshore. Iceland hosted a <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk_Summit" title="Reykjav\xc3\xadk Summit">summit in Reykjav\xc3\xadk in 1986</a> between United States President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and Soviet Premier <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a>, during which they took significant steps toward <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_disarmament" title="Nuclear disarmament">nuclear disarmament</a>. A few years later, Iceland became the first country to recognize the independence of <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> as they <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">broke away</a> from the USSR. Throughout the 1990s, the country expanded its international role and developed a foreign policy oriented toward humanitarian and peacekeeping causes. To that end, Iceland provided aid and expertise to various NATO-led interventions in <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/First_Gulf_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First Gulf War">Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Iceland joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a> in 1994, after which the economy was greatly diversified and liberalised. International economic relations increased further after 2001, when Iceland\'s newly deregulated banks began to raise massive amounts of <a href="/wiki/External_debt" title="External debt">external debt</a>, contributing to a 32% increase in Iceland\'s <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">gross national income</a> between 2002 and 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-jackson_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jackson-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_boom_and_crisis">Economic boom and crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economic boom and crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%932011_Icelandic_financial_crisis" title="2008\xe2\x80\x932011 Icelandic financial crisis">2008\xe2\x80\x932011 Icelandic financial crisis</a> and <a href="/wiki/2009_Icelandic_financial_crisis_protests" title="2009 Icelandic financial crisis protests">2009 Icelandic financial crisis protests</a></div>\n<p>In 2003\xe2\x80\x932007, following the privatisation of the banking sector under the government of <a href="/wiki/Dav%C3%AD%C3%B0_Oddsson" title="Dav\xc3\xad\xc3\xb0 Oddsson">Dav\xc3\xad\xc3\xb0 Oddsson</a>, Iceland moved toward having an economy based on international investment banking and financial services.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewis_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> It was quickly becoming one of the most prosperous countries in the world but was hit hard by a <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%932011_Icelandic_financial_crisis" title="2008\xe2\x80\x932011 Icelandic financial crisis">major financial crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewis_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The crisis resulted in the greatest migration from Iceland since 1887, with a net emigration of 5,000 people in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-nordregio.se_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nordregio.se-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Iceland\'s economy stabilised under the government of <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3hanna_Sigur%C3%B0ard%C3%B3ttir" title="J\xc3\xb3hanna Sigur\xc3\xb0ard\xc3\xb3ttir">J\xc3\xb3hanna Sigur\xc3\xb0ard\xc3\xb3ttir</a>, and grew by 1.6% in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The centre-right <a href="/wiki/Independence_Party_(Iceland)" title="Independence Party (Iceland)">Independence Party</a> was returned to power in coalition with the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Party_(Iceland)" title="Progressive Party (Iceland)">Progressive Party</a> in the 2013 elections.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In the following years, Iceland saw a surge in tourism as the country became a popular holiday destination. In 2016, Prime Minister Sigmundur David Gunnlaugsson resigned after being implicated in the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Papers" title="Panama Papers">Panama Papers</a> scandal.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Early elections in 2016 resulted in a right-wing coalition government of the <a href="/wiki/Independence_Party_(Iceland)" title="Independence Party (Iceland)">Independence Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Reform_Party_(Iceland)" title="Reform Party (Iceland)">Reform Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bright_Future_(Iceland)" title="Bright Future (Iceland)">Bright Future</a>.\n<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> This government fell when Bright Future quit the coalition due to a scandal involving then-Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Bjarni_Benediktsson_(born_1970)" title="Bjarni Benediktsson (born 1970)">Bjarni Benediktsson</a>\'s father\'s letter of support for a convicted paedophile.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Snap elections in October 2017 brought to power a new coalition consisting of the Independence Party, the Progressive Party and the <a href="/wiki/Left-Green_Movement" title="Left-Green Movement">Left-Green Movement</a>, headed by <a href="/wiki/Katr%C3%ADn_Jakobsd%C3%B3ttir" title="Katr\xc3\xadn Jakobsd\xc3\xb3ttir">Katr\xc3\xadn Jakobsd\xc3\xb3ttir</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Iceland.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Map_of_Iceland.svg/220px-Map_of_Iceland.svg.png" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Map_of_Iceland.svg/330px-Map_of_Iceland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Map_of_Iceland.svg/440px-Map_of_Iceland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1834" data-file-height="1489" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Iceland.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>General topographic map</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Iceland" title="Geography of Iceland">Geography of Iceland</a></div>\n<p>Iceland is at the juncture of the North Atlantic and Arctic Oceans. The main island is entirely south of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Circle" title="Arctic Circle">Arctic Circle</a>, which passes through the small Icelandic island of <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%ADmsey" title="Gr\xc3\xadmsey">Gr\xc3\xadmsey</a> off the main island\'s northern coast. The country lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/63rd_parallel_north" title="63rd parallel north">63</a> and <a href="/wiki/68th_parallel_north" title="68th parallel north">68\xc2\xb0N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/25th_meridian_west" title="25th meridian west">25</a> and <a href="/wiki/13th_meridian_west" title="13th meridian west">13\xc2\xb0W</a>.\n</p><p>Iceland is closer to <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a> than to mainland North America, although it is closest to <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> (290&#160;km, 180&#160;mi), an island of North America. Iceland is generally included in Europe for historical, political, cultural, geographical, and practical reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-Ingebritsen2000_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ingebritsen2000-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LehtiSmith2003_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LehtiSmith2003-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Miles2005_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miles2005-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dhondt2011_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dhondt2011-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Geologically, the island includes parts of both continental plates. The closest bodies of land in Europe are the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a> (420&#160;km, 260&#160;mi); <a href="/wiki/Jan_Mayen" title="Jan Mayen">Jan Mayen</a> Island (570&#160;km, 350&#160;mi); <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Hebrides" title="Outer Hebrides">Outer Hebrides</a>, both about 740&#160;km (460&#160;mi); and the Scottish mainland and <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a>, both about 750&#160;km (470&#160;mi). The nearest part of Continental Europe is mainland Norway, about 970&#160;km (600&#160;mi) away, while mainland North America is 2,070&#160;km (1,290&#160;mi) away, at the northern tip of <a href="/wiki/Labrador" title="Labrador">Labrador</a>. \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Icelandic_landscapes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Icelandic_landscapes.jpg/220px-Icelandic_landscapes.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Icelandic_landscapes.jpg/330px-Icelandic_landscapes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Icelandic_landscapes.jpg/440px-Icelandic_landscapes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8192" data-file-height="5568" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Icelandic_landscapes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Three typical Icelandic landscapes</div></div></div>\n<p>Iceland is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">world\'s 18th largest island</a>, and Europe\'s second-largest island after Great Britain. The main island is 101,826&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (39,315&#160;sq&#160;mi), but the entire country is 103,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (40,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) in size, of which 62.7% is <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a>. About 30 minor islands are in Iceland, including the lightly populated Gr\xc3\xadmsey and the <a href="/wiki/Vestmannaeyjar" title="Vestmannaeyjar">Vestmannaeyjar</a> archipelago. Lakes and glaciers cover 14.3% of its surface; only 23% is vegetated.<sup id="cite_ref-NLS_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NLS-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The largest lakes are <a href="/wiki/%C3%9E%C3%B3risvatn" title="\xc3\x9e\xc3\xb3risvatn">\xc3\x9e\xc3\xb3risvatn</a> reservoir: 83\xe2\x80\x9388&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (32\xe2\x80\x9334&#160;sq&#160;mi) and <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Eingvallavatn" title="\xc3\x9eingvallavatn">\xc3\x9eingvallavatn</a>: 82&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (32&#160;sq&#160;mi); other important lakes include <a href="/wiki/Lagarflj%C3%B3t" title="Lagarflj\xc3\xb3t">Lagarflj\xc3\xb3t</a> and <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BDvatn" title="M\xc3\xbdvatn">M\xc3\xbdvatn</a>. <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B6kuls%C3%A1rl%C3%B3n" title="J\xc3\xb6kuls\xc3\xa1rl\xc3\xb3n">J\xc3\xb6kuls\xc3\xa1rl\xc3\xb3n</a> is the deepest lake, at 248&#160;m (814&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Geologically, Iceland is part of the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_Ridge" title="Mid-Atlantic Ridge">Mid-Atlantic Ridge</a>, a ridge along which the <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_crust" title="Oceanic crust">oceanic crust</a> spreads and forms new oceanic crust. This part of the mid-ocean ridge is located above a mantle plume, causing Iceland to be <a href="/wiki/Subaerial" title="Subaerial">subaerial</a> (above the surface of the sea). The ridge marks the boundary between the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Plate" title="Eurasian Plate">Eurasian</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_American_Plate" title="North American Plate">North American Plates</a>, and Iceland was created by <a href="/wiki/Rift" title="Rift">rifting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Accretion_(geology)" title="Accretion (geology)">accretion</a> through volcanism along the ridge.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many <a href="/wiki/Fjord" title="Fjord">fjords</a> punctuate Iceland\'s 4,970-km-long (3,088-mi) coastline, which is also where most settlements are situated. The island\'s interior, the <a href="/wiki/Highlands_of_Iceland" title="Highlands of Iceland">Highlands of Iceland</a>, is a cold and uninhabitable combination of sand, mountains, and <a href="/wiki/Lava_field" title="Lava field">lava fields</a>. The major towns are the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjav\xc3\xadk">Reykjav\xc3\xadk</a>, along with its outlying towns of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B3pavogur" title="K\xc3\xb3pavogur">K\xc3\xb3pavogur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hafnarfj%C3%B6r%C3%B0ur" title="Hafnarfj\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb0ur">Hafnarfj\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb0ur</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gar%C3%B0ab%C3%A6r" title="Gar\xc3\xb0ab\xc3\xa6r">Gar\xc3\xb0ab\xc3\xa6r</a>, nearby <a href="/wiki/Reykjanesb%C3%A6r" title="Reykjanesb\xc3\xa6r">Reykjanesb\xc3\xa6r</a> where the international airport is located, and the town of <a href="/wiki/Akureyri" title="Akureyri">Akureyri</a> in northern Iceland. The island of Gr\xc3\xadmsey on the Arctic Circle contains the northernmost habitation of Iceland, whereas <a href="/wiki/Kolbeinsey" title="Kolbeinsey">Kolbeinsey</a> contains the northernmost point of Iceland.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Govt_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Govt-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Iceland has <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Iceland" title="List of national parks of Iceland">three national parks</a>: <a href="/wiki/Vatnaj%C3%B6kull_National_Park" title="Vatnaj\xc3\xb6kull National Park">Vatnaj\xc3\xb6kull National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sn%C3%A6fellsj%C3%B6kull" title="Sn\xc3\xa6fellsj\xc3\xb6kull">Sn\xc3\xa6fellsj\xc3\xb6kull National Park</a>, and <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Eingvellir" title="\xc3\x9eingvellir">\xc3\x9eingvellir National Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The country is considered a "strong performer" in environmental protection, having been ranked 13th in <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>\'s Environmental Performance Index of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<center>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 158px"><div style="width: Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 181.33333333333px"><div style="width: 181.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" data-file-height="2592" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Landscape as seen from <a href="/wiki/Laugavegur" title="Laugavegur">Laugavegur</a> hiking trail\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n</center>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Iceland" title="Geology of Iceland">Geology of Iceland</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Iceland_plume" title="Iceland plume">Iceland plume</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Erupting_geysir.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Erupting_geysir.jpg/220px-Erupting_geysir.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Erupting_geysir.jpg/330px-Erupting_geysir.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Erupting_geysir.jpg/440px-Erupting_geysir.jpg 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Erupting_geysir.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The erupting <a href="/wiki/Geysir" title="Geysir">Geysir</a> in <a href="/wiki/Haukadalur" title="Haukadalur">Haukadalur</a> valley, the oldest known <a href="/wiki/Geyser" title="Geyser">geyser</a> in the world</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gullfoss,_an_iconic_waterfall_of_Iceland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Gullfoss%2C_an_iconic_waterfall_of_Iceland.jpg/220px-Gullfoss%2C_an_iconic_waterfall_of_Iceland.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Gullfoss%2C_an_iconic_waterfall_of_Iceland.jpg/330px-Gullfoss%2C_an_iconic_waterfall_of_Iceland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Gullfoss%2C_an_iconic_waterfall_of_Iceland.jpg/440px-Gullfoss%2C_an_iconic_waterfall_of_Iceland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gullfoss,_an_iconic_waterfall_of_Iceland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gullfoss" title="Gullfoss">Gullfoss</a>, an iconic waterfall of Iceland</div></div></div>\n<p>A geologically young land, Iceland is located on both the <a href="/wiki/Iceland_hotspot" title="Iceland hotspot">Iceland hotspot</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_Ridge" title="Mid-Atlantic Ridge">Mid-Atlantic Ridge</a>, which runs right through it. This location means that the island is highly geologically active with many volcanoes, notably <a href="/wiki/Hekla" title="Hekla">Hekla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eldgj%C3%A1" title="Eldgj\xc3\xa1">Eldgj\xc3\xa1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Her%C3%B0ubrei%C3%B0" title="Her\xc3\xb0ubrei\xc3\xb0">Her\xc3\xb0ubrei\xc3\xb0</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eldfell" title="Eldfell">Eldfell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The volcanic eruption of <a href="/wiki/Laki" title="Laki">Laki</a> in 1783\xe2\x80\x931784 caused a famine that killed nearly a quarter of the island\'s population.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In addition, the eruption caused dust clouds and haze to appear over most of Europe and parts of Asia and Africa for several months afterward, and affected climates in other areas.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Iceland has many <a href="/wiki/Geyser" title="Geyser">geysers</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Geysir" title="Geysir">Geysir</a>, from which the English word is derived, and the famous <a href="/wiki/Strokkur" title="Strokkur">Strokkur</a>, which erupts every 8\xe2\x80\x9310&#160;minutes. After a phase of inactivity, Geysir started erupting again after a <a href="/wiki/2000_Iceland_earthquakes" title="2000 Iceland earthquakes">series of earthquakes in 2000</a>. Geysir has since grown quieter and does not erupt often.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With the widespread availability of <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_power" title="Geothermal power">geothermal power</a>, and the harnessing of many rivers and waterfalls for <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a>, most residents have access to inexpensive hot water, heating, and electricity. The island is composed primarily of <a href="/wiki/Basalt" title="Basalt">basalt</a>, a low-<a href="/wiki/Silica" class="mw-redirect" title="Silica">silica</a> lava associated with <a href="/wiki/Effusive_eruption" title="Effusive eruption">effusive volcanism</a> as has occurred also in <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>. Iceland, however, has a variety of volcanic types (composite and fissure), many producing more evolved lavas such as <a href="/wiki/Rhyolite" title="Rhyolite">rhyolite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andesite" title="Andesite">andesite</a>. Iceland has hundreds of volcanoes with about 30 active volcanic systems.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Surtsey" title="Surtsey">Surtsey</a>, one of the youngest islands in the world, is part of Iceland. Named after <a href="/wiki/Surtr" title="Surtr">Surtr</a>, it rose above the ocean in a series of volcanic eruptions between 8 November 1963 and 5 June 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Govt_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Govt-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Only scientists researching the growth of new life are allowed to visit the island.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 21 March 2010, a <a href="/wiki/2010_eruptions_of_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull" title="2010 eruptions of Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull">volcano in Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull</a> in the south of Iceland erupted for the first time since 1821, forcing 600 people to flee their homes.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Additional eruptions on 14 April forced hundreds of people to abandon their homes.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The resultant cloud of <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_ash" title="Volcanic ash">volcanic ash</a> brought <a href="/wiki/Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption" title="Air travel disruption after the 2010 Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull eruption">major disruption to air travel</a> across Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Iceland_gif.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Iceland_gif.gif/220px-Iceland_gif.gif" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Iceland_gif.gif/330px-Iceland_gif.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Iceland_gif.gif/440px-Iceland_gif.gif 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iceland_gif.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>High-field overview of area around Reykir</div></div></div>\n<p>Another large eruption occurred on 21 May 2011. This time it was the <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%ADmsv%C3%B6tn" title="Gr\xc3\xadmsv\xc3\xb6tn">Gr\xc3\xadmsv\xc3\xb6tn</a> volcano, located under the thick ice of Europe\'s largest glacier, <a href="/wiki/Vatnaj%C3%B6kull" title="Vatnaj\xc3\xb6kull">Vatnaj\xc3\xb6kull</a>. Gr\xc3\xadmsv\xc3\xb6tn is one of Iceland\'s most active volcanoes, and this eruption was much more powerful than the 2010 Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull activity, with ash and lava hurled 20&#160;km (12&#160;mi) into the atmosphere, creating a large cloud.<sup id="cite_ref-connor_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-connor-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The highest elevation for Iceland is listed as 2,110 m (6,923&#160;ft) at <a href="/wiki/Hvannadalshn%C3%BAkur" title="Hvannadalshn\xc3\xbakur">Hvannadalshn\xc3\xbakur</a> (64\xc2\xb000\xe2\x80\xb2N 16\xc2\xb039\xe2\x80\xb2W).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:508px;max-width:508px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Iceland_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Iceland_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/200px-Iceland_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png" width="200" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Iceland_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/300px-Iceland_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Iceland_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/400px-Iceland_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="765" data-file-height="765" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</a> types of Iceland</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull.jpeg/300px-Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull.jpeg" width="300" height="201" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull.jpeg/450px-Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull.jpeg/600px-Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2960" data-file-height="1983" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull" title="Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull">Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull</a> glacier, one of the smaller <a href="/wiki/Glaciers_of_Iceland" class="mw-redirect" title="Glaciers of Iceland">glaciers of Iceland</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Iceland" title="Climate of Iceland">Climate of Iceland</a></div>\n<p>The climate of Iceland\'s coast is <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic</a>. The warm <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Current" title="North Atlantic Current">North Atlantic Current</a> ensures generally higher annual temperatures than in most places of similar latitude in the world. Regions in the world with similar climates include the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Peninsula" title="Alaska Peninsula">Alaska Peninsula</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tierra_del_Fuego" title="Tierra del Fuego">Tierra del Fuego</a>, although these regions are closer to the equator. Despite its proximity to the Arctic, the island\'s coasts remain ice-free through the winter. Ice incursions are rare, the last having occurred on the north coast in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The climate varies between different parts of the island. Generally speaking, the south coast is warmer, wetter, and windier than the north. The Central Highlands are the coldest part of the country. Low-lying inland areas in the north are the most arid. Snowfall in winter is more common in the north than the south.\n</p><p>The highest air temperature recorded was 30.5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (86.9&#160;\xc2\xb0F) on 22 June 1939 at Teigarhorn on the southeastern coast. The lowest was \xe2\x88\x9238&#160;\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x9236.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F) on 22 January 1918 at Gr\xc3\xadmssta\xc3\xb0ir and M\xc3\xb6\xc3\xb0rudalur in the northeastern hinterland. The temperature records for Reykjav\xc3\xadk are 26.2&#160;\xc2\xb0C (79.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F) on 30 July 2008, and \xe2\x88\x9224.5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x9212.1&#160;\xc2\xb0F) on 21 January 1918.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="14">Climate data for <a
