class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Whaling_in_Iceland" title="Whaling in Iceland">Whaling in Iceland</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Botany_of_Iceland" title="The Botany of Iceland">The Botany of Iceland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alopex_lagopus_IMG_9019.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Alopex_lagopus_IMG_9019.JPG/220px-Alopex_lagopus_IMG_9019.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Alopex_lagopus_IMG_9019.JPG/330px-Alopex_lagopus_IMG_9019.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Alopex_lagopus_IMG_9019.JPG/440px-Alopex_lagopus_IMG_9019.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5015" data-file-height="3343" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alopex_lagopus_IMG_9019.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Arctic_fox" title="Arctic fox">Arctic fox</a> is the only indigenous land mammal in Iceland and was the only land mammal prior to the arrival of humans</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Icelandic_sheep_summer_06.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Icelandic_sheep_summer_06.jpg/220px-Icelandic_sheep_summer_06.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Icelandic_sheep_summer_06.jpg/330px-Icelandic_sheep_summer_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Icelandic_sheep_summer_06.jpg/440px-Icelandic_sheep_summer_06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="795" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Icelandic_sheep_summer_06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_sheep" title="Icelandic sheep">Icelandic sheep</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Icelandic_Horse_with_blue_eyes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Icelandic_Horse_with_blue_eyes.jpg/220px-Icelandic_Horse_with_blue_eyes.jpg" width="220" height="324" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Icelandic_Horse_with_blue_eyes.jpg/330px-Icelandic_Horse_with_blue_eyes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Icelandic_Horse_with_blue_eyes.jpg/440px-Icelandic_Horse_with_blue_eyes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4540" data-file-height="6692" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Icelandic_Horse_with_blue_eyes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_horse" title="Icelandic horse">Icelandic horse</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Around 1,300 species of insects are known in Iceland. This is low compared with other countries (over one million species have been described worldwide). Iceland is essentially free of mosquitoes.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The only native land mammal when humans arrived was the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_fox" title="Arctic fox">Arctic fox</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-wildlife_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wildlife-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> which came to the island at the end of the ice age, walking over the frozen sea. On rare occasions, bats have been carried to the island with the winds, but they are not able to breed there. <a href="/wiki/Polar_bears" class="mw-redirect" title="Polar bears">Polar bears</a> occasionally come over from <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, but they are just visitors, and no Icelandic populations exist.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> No native or free-living reptiles or amphibians are on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, Iceland belongs to the Arctic province of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. Around three-quarters of the island is barren of vegetation; plant life consists mainly of grassland, which is regularly grazed by livestock. The most common tree native to Iceland is the northern birch (<i><a href="/wiki/Betula_pubescens" title="Betula pubescens">Betula pubescens</a></i>), which formerly formed forests over much of Iceland, along with aspens (<i><a href="/wiki/Populus_tremula" title="Populus tremula">Populus tremula</a></i>), rowans (<i><a href="/wiki/Sorbus_aucuparia" title="Sorbus aucuparia">Sorbus aucuparia</a></i>), common junipers (<i><a href="/wiki/Juniperus_communis" title="Juniperus communis">Juniperus communis</a></i>), and other smaller trees, mainly willows.\n</p><p>When the island was first settled, it was extensively forested. In the late 12th century, <a href="/wiki/Ari_the_Wise" class="mw-redirect" title="Ari the Wise">Ari the Wise</a> described it in the <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Dslendingab%C3%B3k" title="\xc3\x8dslendingab\xc3\xb3k">\xc3\x8dslendingab\xc3\xb3k</a> as "forested from mountain to sea shore".<sup id="cite_ref-Dirt_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dirt-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Permanent human settlement greatly disturbed the isolated ecosystem of thin, volcanic soils and limited <a href="/wiki/Species_richness" title="Species richness">species diversity</a>. The forests were heavily exploited over the centuries for firewood and timber.<sup id="cite_ref-wildlife_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wildlife-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">Deforestation</a>, climatic deterioration during the <a href="/wiki/Little_Ice_Age" title="Little Ice Age">Little Ice Age</a>, and overgrazing by sheep imported by settlers caused a loss of critical topsoil due to <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">erosion</a>. Today, many farms have been abandoned. Three-quarters of Iceland\'s 100,000 square kilometres is affected by soil erosion, 18,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (6,900&#160;sq&#160;mi) serious enough to make the land useless.<sup id="cite_ref-Dirt_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dirt-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Only a few small birch stands now exist in isolated reserves. The planting of new forests has increased the number of trees, but the result does not compare to the original forests. Some of the planted forests include <a href="/wiki/Introduced_species" title="Introduced species">introduced species</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wildlife_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wildlife-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The tallest tree in Iceland is a <a href="/wiki/Sitka_spruce" class="mw-redirect" title="Sitka spruce">sitka spruce</a> planted in 1949 in <a href="/wiki/Kirkjub%C3%A6jarklaustur" title="Kirkjub\xc3\xa6jarklaustur">Kirkjub\xc3\xa6jarklaustur</a>; it was measured at 25.2&#160;m (83&#160;ft) in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The animals of Iceland include the <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_sheep" title="Icelandic sheep">Icelandic sheep</a>, <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_cattle" title="Icelandic cattle">cattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_chicken" class="mw-redirect" title="Icelandic chicken">chickens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_goat" title="Icelandic goat">goats</a>, the sturdy <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_horse" title="Icelandic horse">Icelandic horse</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_Sheepdog" title="Icelandic Sheepdog">Icelandic Sheepdog</a>, all descendants of animals imported by Europeans. Wild mammals include the Arctic fox, <a href="/wiki/Mink" title="Mink">mink</a>, mice, rats, rabbits, and <a href="/wiki/Reindeer" title="Reindeer">reindeer</a>. Polar bears occasionally visit the island, travelling on icebergs from Greenland. In June 2008, two polar bears arrived in the same month.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marine_mammals" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine mammals">Marine mammals</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Grey_seal" title="Grey seal">grey seal</a> (<i>Halichoerus grypus</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Harbor_seal" title="Harbor seal">harbor seal</a> (<i>Phoca vitulina</i>). Many species of fish live in the ocean waters surrounding Iceland, and the <a href="/wiki/Fishing_industry" title="Fishing industry">fishing industry</a> is a major part of Iceland\'s economy, accounting for roughly half of the country\'s total exports. Birds, especially seabirds, are an important part of Iceland\'s animal life. <a href="/wiki/Puffin" title="Puffin">Puffins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skua" title="Skua">skuas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kittiwake" title="Kittiwake">kittiwakes</a> nest on its sea cliffs.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Commercial_whaling" class="mw-redirect" title="Commercial whaling">Commercial whaling</a> is practised intermittently<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> along with scientific whale hunts.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Whale watching has become an important part of Iceland\'s economy since 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Iceland" title="Politics of Iceland">Politics of Iceland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Politics_Of_Iceland.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Politics_Of_Iceland.svg/450px-Politics_Of_Iceland.svg.png" width="450" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Politics_Of_Iceland.svg/675px-Politics_Of_Iceland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Politics_Of_Iceland.svg/900px-Politics_Of_Iceland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Politics_Of_Iceland.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The political system of Iceland</div></div></div>\n<p>Iceland has a <a href="/wiki/Left%E2%80%93right_politics" class="mw-redirect" title="Left\xe2\x80\x93right politics">left\xe2\x80\x93right</a> <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_parliamentary_election,_2017" title="Icelandic parliamentary election, 2017">2017 parliamentary election</a>, the biggest parties are the centre-right <a href="/wiki/Independence_Party_(Iceland)" title="Independence Party (Iceland)">Independence Party</a> (<i>Sj\xc3\xa1lfst\xc3\xa6\xc3\xb0isflokkurinn</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Left-Green_Movement" title="Left-Green Movement">Left-Green Movement</a> (<i>Vinstrihreyfingin&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 gr\xc3\xa6nt frambo\xc3\xb0</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Party_(Iceland)" title="Progressive Party (Iceland)">Progressive Party</a> (<i>Frams\xc3\xb3knarflokkurinn</i>). These three parties form the current ruling coalition in the cabinet led by leftist <a href="/wiki/Katr%C3%ADn_Jakobsd%C3%B3ttir" title="Katr\xc3\xadn Jakobsd\xc3\xb3ttir">Katr\xc3\xadn Jakobsd\xc3\xb3ttir</a>.\nOther political parties with seats in the <a href="/wiki/Althing" title="Althing">Althing</a> (Parliament) are the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Alliance" title="Social Democratic Alliance">Social Democratic Alliance</a> (<i>Samfylkingin</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Centre_Party_(Iceland)" title="Centre Party (Iceland)">Centre Party</a> (<i>Mi\xc3\xb0flokkurinn</i>), Iceland\'s <a href="/wiki/Pirate_Party_(Iceland)" title="Pirate Party (Iceland)">Pirates</a>, the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Iceland,_2016)" title="People&#39;s Party (Iceland, 2016)">People\'s Party</a> (<i>Flokkur f\xc3\xb3lksins</i>), and the <a href="/wiki/Reform_Party_(Iceland)" title="Reform Party (Iceland)">Reform Party</a> (<i>Vi\xc3\xb0reisn</i>).\n</p><p>Iceland was the first country in the world to have a political party formed and led entirely by women.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Known as the Women\'s List or Women\'s Alliance (<i>Kvennalistinn</i>), it was founded in 1983 to advance the political, economic, and social needs of women. After participating in its first parliamentary elections, the Women\'s List helped increase the proportion of female parliamentarians by 15%.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Although it disbanded in 1999, merging with the Social Democratic Alliance, it left a lasting influence on Iceland\'s politics: every major party has a 40% quota for women, and in 2009 nearly a third of members of parliament were female, compared to the global average of 16%.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Following the 2016 elections, 48% of members of parliament are female.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016 Iceland was ranked 2nd in the strength of its democratic institutions<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and 13th in government transparency.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The country has a high level of civic participation, with 81.4% voter turnout during the most recent elections,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> compared to an OECD average of 72%. However, only 50% of Icelanders say they trust their political institutions, slightly less than the OECD average of 56% (and most probably a consequence of the political scandals in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Icelandic financial crisis">Icelandic financial crisis</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Iceland_\xe2\x80\x93_OECD_Better_Life_Index_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iceland_\xe2\x80\x93_OECD_Better_Life_Index-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Iceland" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Iceland">Government of Iceland</a></div>\n <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Althingishusid.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Althingishusid.jpg/200px-Althingishusid.jpg" width="200" height="132" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Althingishusid.jpg/300px-Althingishusid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Althingishusid.jpg/400px-Althingishusid.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="463" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Althing" title="Althing">Parliament of Iceland</a> in <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjav\xc3\xadk">Reykjav\xc3\xadk</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Iceland-Reykjavik-Stjornarrad-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Iceland-Reykjavik-Stjornarrad-1.jpg/200px-Iceland-Reykjavik-Stjornarrad-1.jpg" width="200" height="110" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Iceland-Reykjavik-Stjornarrad-1.jpg/300px-Iceland-Reykjavik-Stjornarrad-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Iceland-Reykjavik-Stjornarrad-1.jpg/400px-Iceland-Reykjavik-Stjornarrad-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3020" data-file-height="1661" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Iceland" title="Cabinet of Iceland">Cabinet of Iceland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Iceland" title="Prime Minister of Iceland">Prime Minister\'s Office</a> in <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjav\xc3\xadk">Reykjav\xc3\xadk</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Law_speaker.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Law_speaker.jpg/220px-Law_speaker.jpg" width="220" height="284" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Law_speaker.jpg/330px-Law_speaker.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/44/Law_speaker.jpg 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="452" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Law_speaker.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 19th-century depiction of the <a href="/wiki/Al%C3%BEingi" class="mw-redirect" title="Al\xc3\xbeingi">Al\xc3\xbeingi</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_Commonwealth" title="Icelandic Commonwealth">Commonwealth</a> in session at <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Eingvellir" title="\xc3\x9eingvellir">\xc3\x9eingvellir</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Iceland is a <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>. The modern parliament, <i>Al\xc3\xbeingi</i> (English: <a href="/wiki/Althing" title="Althing">Althing</a>), was founded in 1845 as an advisory body to the Danish monarch. It was widely seen as a re-establishment of the assembly founded in 930 in the <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_Commonwealth" title="Icelandic Commonwealth">Commonwealth</a> period and suspended in 1799. Consequently, "it is arguably the world\'s oldest <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary democracy</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> It currently has 63 members, elected for a maximum period of four years.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The president is elected by popular vote for a term of four years, with no term limit. The elections for president, the Althing, and local municipal councils are all held separately every four years.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Iceland" title="President of Iceland">president of Iceland</a> is a largely ceremonial head of state and serves as a diplomat, but may veto laws voted by the parliament and put them to a national referendum.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The current president is <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%B0ni_Th._J%C3%B3hannesson" title="Gu\xc3\xb0ni Th. J\xc3\xb3hannesson">Gu\xc3\xb0ni Th. J\xc3\xb3hannesson</a>. The head of government is the prime minister who, together with the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Iceland" title="Cabinet of Iceland">cabinet</a>, is responsible for <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a> government. The cabinet is appointed by the president after a general election to the Althing; however, the appointment is usually negotiated by the leaders of the political parties, who decide among themselves after discussions which parties can form the cabinet and how to distribute its seats, under the condition that it has a majority support in the Althing. Only when the party leaders are unable to reach a conclusion by themselves within a reasonable time span does the president exercise this power and appoint the cabinet personally. This has not happened since the republic was founded in 1944, but in 1942 regent <a href="/wiki/Sveinn_Bj%C3%B6rnsson" title="Sveinn Bj\xc3\xb6rnsson">Sveinn Bj\xc3\xb6rnsson</a>, who had been installed in that position by the Althing in 1941, appointed a non-parliamentary government. The regent had, for all practical purposes, the position of a president, and Sveinn would later become the country\'s first president in 1944.\n</p><p>The governments of Iceland have always been coalition governments, with two or more parties involved, as no single political party has ever received a majority of seats in the Althing throughout the republican period. The extent of the political power possessed by the office of the president is disputed by legal scholars<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (June 2016)">which?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, in Iceland; several provisions of the constitution appear to give the president some important powers, but other provisions and traditions suggest differently.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 1980, Icelanders elected <a href="/wiki/Vigd%C3%ADs_Finnbogad%C3%B3ttir" title="Vigd\xc3\xads Finnbogad\xc3\xb3ttir">Vigd\xc3\xads Finnbogad\xc3\xb3ttir</a> as president, the world\'s first directly elected female head of state. She retired from office in 1996. In 2009, Iceland became the first country with an openly gay head of government when <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3hanna_Sigur%C3%B0ard%C3%B3ttir" title="J\xc3\xb3hanna Sigur\xc3\xb0ard\xc3\xb3ttir">J\xc3\xb3hanna Sigur\xc3\xb0ard\xc3\xb3ttir</a> became prime minister.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Iceland" title="Administrative divisions of Iceland">Administrative divisions of Iceland</a></div>\n<p>Iceland is divided into regions, constituencies and municipalities. The eight regions are primarily used for statistical purposes. District court jurisdictions also use an older version of this division.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Govt_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Govt-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Until 2003, the constituencies for the parliamentary elections were the same as the regions, but by an amendment to the constitution, they were changed to the current six constituencies:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Constituencies_of_Iceland" title="Constituencies of Iceland">Reykjav\xc3\xadk North</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Constituencies_of_Iceland" title="Constituencies of Iceland">Reykjav\xc3\xadk South</a></i> (city regions);</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Constituencies_of_Iceland" title="Constituencies of Iceland">Southwest</a></i> (four <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">non-contiguous</a> suburban areas around Reykjav\xc3\xadk);</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Constituencies_of_Iceland" title="Constituencies of Iceland">Northwest</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Constituencies_of_Iceland" title="Constituencies of Iceland">Northeast</a></i> (northern half of Iceland, split); and,</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Constituencies_of_Iceland" title="Constituencies of Iceland">South</a></i> (southern half of Iceland, excluding Reykjav\xc3\xadk and suburbs).</li></ul></dd></dl>\n<p>The redistricting change was made to balance the weight of different districts of the country, since previously a vote cast in the sparsely populated areas around the country would count much more than a vote cast in the Reykjav\xc3\xadk city area. The imbalance between districts has been reduced by the new system, but still exists.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Govt_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Govt-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>74 municipalities in Iceland govern local matters like schools, transport, and zoning.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> These are the actual <a href="/wiki/Administrative_division" title="Administrative division">second-level subdivisions</a> of Iceland, as the constituencies have no relevance except in elections and for statistical purposes. Reykjav\xc3\xadk is by far the most populous municipality, about four times more populous than <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B3pavogur" title="K\xc3\xb3pavogur">K\xc3\xb3pavogur</a>, the second one.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Govt_59-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Govt-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<center>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 165.33333333333px"><div style="width: 165.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 163.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Iceland.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Regions_of_Iceland.png/245px-Regions_of_Iceland.png" width="164" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Regions_of_Iceland.png/367px-Regions_of_Iceland.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Regions_of_Iceland.png/489px-Regions_of_Iceland.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="589" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Iceland" title="Regions of Iceland">Regions of Iceland</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 165.33333333333px"><div style="width: 165.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 163.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Constituencies_Iceland.png"
