//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Sta%C3%B0arbakkakirkja.jpg/440px-Sta%C3%B0arbakkakirkja.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1582" data-file-height="1336" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sta%C3%B0arbakkakirkja.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A church in the northwest of Iceland</div></div></div>\n<p>Icelanders have freedom of religion guaranteed under the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Iceland" title="Constitution of Iceland">Constitution</a>, although the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Iceland" title="Church of Iceland">Church of Iceland</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a> body, is the <a href="/wiki/State_church" class="mw-redirect" title="State church">state church</a>:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The Evangelical Lutheran Church shall be the State Church in Iceland and, as such, it shall be supported and protected by the State.</p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite>Article 62, Section IV of <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Iceland" title="Constitution of Iceland">Constitution of Iceland</a><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>The Registers Iceland keeps account of the religious affiliation of every Icelandic citizen. In 2017, Icelanders were divided into religious groups as follows:\n</p>\n<ul><li>67.22% members of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Iceland" title="Church of Iceland">Church of Iceland</a>;</li>\n<li>11.56% members of other <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> denomination;</li>\n<li>11.29% other religions and not specified;</li>\n<li>6.69% unaffiliated;</li>\n<li>1.19% members of <a href="/wiki/Heathenism_(new_religious_movement)" class="mw-redirect" title="Heathenism (new religious movement)">Germanic Heathen</a> groups (99% of them belonging to <a href="/wiki/%C3%81satr%C3%BAarf%C3%A9lagi%C3%B0" title="\xc3\x81satr\xc3\xbaarf\xc3\xa9lagi\xc3\xb0">\xc3\x81satr\xc3\xbaarf\xc3\xa9lagi\xc3\xb0</a>);</li>\n<li>0.67% members of the <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_Ethical_Humanist_Association" title="Icelandic Ethical Humanist Association">Icelandic Ethical Humanist Association</a>;</li>\n<li>0.55% members of <a href="/wiki/Zuism" title="Zuism">Zuist</a> groups.</li></ul>\n<p>Iceland is a very <a href="/wiki/Secular" class="mw-redirect" title="Secular">secular</a> country; as with other Nordic nations, religious attendance is relatively low.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> The above statistics represent administrative membership of religious organisations, which does not necessarily reflect the belief demographics of the population. According to a study published in 2001, 23% of the inhabitants were either <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheist</a> or <a href="/wiki/Agnosticism" title="Agnosticism">agnostic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> A Gallup poll conducted in 2012 found that 57% of Icelanders considered themselves "religious", 31% considered themselves "non-religious", while 10% defined themselves as "convinced atheists", placing Iceland among the ten countries with the highest proportions of atheists in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Religion-and-Atheism_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Religion-and-Atheism-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> The proportion registered in the official Church of Iceland is declining rapidly, more than 1% per year (the Church of Iceland has declined from 80% in 2010 to less than 70% in 2017).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Iceland" title="Culture of Iceland">Culture of Iceland</a></div>\n<p>Icelandic culture has its roots in North Germanic traditions. <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_literature" title="Icelandic literature">Icelandic literature</a> is popular, in particular the <a href="/wiki/Sagas_of_Icelanders" title="Sagas of Icelanders">sagas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edda" title="Edda">eddas</a> that were written during the <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">High</a> and <a href="/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages" title="Late Middle Ages">Late Middle Ages</a>. Centuries of isolation have helped to insulate the country\'s Nordic culture from external influence; a prominent example is the preservation of the <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic language</a>, which remains the closest to Old Norse of all modern Nordic languages.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In contrast to other Nordic countries, Icelanders place relatively great importance on independence and self-sufficiency; in a public opinion analysis conducted by the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, over 85% of Icelanders believe independence is "very important," compared to 47% of Norwegians, 49% of Danes, and an average of 53% for the EU25.<sup id="cite_ref-europeancommission_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europeancommission-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> Icelanders also have a very strong work ethic, working some of the longest hours of any industrialised nation.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to a poll conducted by the OECD, 66% of Icelanders were satisfied with their lives, while 70% believed that their lives will be satisfying in the future. Similarly, 83% reported having more positive experiences in an average day than negative ones, compared to an OECD average of 72%, which makes Iceland one of the <a href="/wiki/Happiest_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Happiest country">happiest countries</a> in the OECD.<sup id="cite_ref-Iceland_\xe2\x80\x93_OECD_Better_Life_Index_94-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iceland_\xe2\x80\x93_OECD_Better_Life_Index-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> A more recent 2012 survey found that around three quarters of respondents stated they were satisfied with their lives, compared to a global average of about 53%.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Iceland is liberal with regard to <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> rights issues. In 1996, the Icelandic parliament passed legislation to create <a href="/wiki/Registered_partnership" class="mw-redirect" title="Registered partnership">registered partnerships</a> for same-sex couples, conferring nearly all the rights and benefits of marriage. In 2006, parliament voted unanimously to grant same-sex couples the same rights as heterosexual couples in adoption, parenting and assisted insemination treatment. On 11 June 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Iceland" title="Same-sex marriage in Iceland">Icelandic parliament amended the marriage law</a>, making it gender neutral and defining marriage as between two individuals, making Iceland one of the first countries in the world to legalise <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriages</a>. The law took effect on 27 June 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-gaymarriage_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gaymarriage-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> The amendment to the law also means registered partnerships for same-sex couples are now no longer possible, and marriage is their only option\xe2\x80\x94identical to the existing situation for opposite-sex couples.<sup id="cite_ref-gaymarriage_216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gaymarriage-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Icelanders are known for their deep sense of community: An OECD survey found that 98% believe they know someone they could rely on in a time of need, higher than in any other industrialised country. Similarly, only 6% reported "rarely" or "never" socializing with others.<sup id="cite_ref-Iceland_\xe2\x80\x93_OECD_Better_Life_Index_94-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iceland_\xe2\x80\x93_OECD_Better_Life_Index-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> This high level of social cohesion is attributed to the small size and homogeneity of the population, as well as to a long history of harsh survival in an isolated environment, which reinforced the importance of unity and cooperation.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">Egalitarianism</a> is highly valued among the people of Iceland, with income inequality being among the lowest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The constitution explicitly prohibits the enactment of noble privileges, titles, and ranks.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated60_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated60-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> Everyone is addressed by their first name. As in other Nordic countries, equality between the sexes is very high; Iceland is consistently ranked among the top three countries in the world for women to live in.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_literature" title="Icelandic literature">Icelandic literature</a></div><p>In 2011, Reykjavik was designated a UNESCO City of Literature.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:M%C3%B6%C3%B0ruvallab%C3%B3k_f13r.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/M%C3%B6%C3%B0ruvallab%C3%B3k_f13r.jpg/220px-M%C3%B6%C3%B0ruvallab%C3%B3k_f13r.jpg" width="220" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/M%C3%B6%C3%B0ruvallab%C3%B3k_f13r.jpg/330px-M%C3%B6%C3%B0ruvallab%C3%B3k_f13r.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/M%C3%B6%C3%B0ruvallab%C3%B3k_f13r.jpg/440px-M%C3%B6%C3%B0ruvallab%C3%B3k_f13r.jpg 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="491" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:M%C3%B6%C3%B0ruvallab%C3%B3k_f13r.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A page of <a href="/wiki/Nj%C3%A1ls_saga" title="Nj\xc3\xa1ls saga">Nj\xc3\xa1ls saga</a> from <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6%C3%B0ruvallab%C3%B3k" title="M\xc3\xb6\xc3\xb0ruvallab\xc3\xb3k">M\xc3\xb6\xc3\xb0ruvallab\xc3\xb3k</a>. The sagas are a significant part of the Icelandic heritage</div></div></div>\n<p>Iceland\'s best-known classical works of literature are the <a href="/wiki/Icelanders%27_sagas" class="mw-redirect" title="Icelanders&#39; sagas">Icelanders\' sagas</a>, prose epics set in Iceland\'s age of settlement. The most famous of these include <i><a href="/wiki/Nj%C3%A1ls_saga" title="Nj\xc3\xa1ls saga">Nj\xc3\xa1ls saga</a></i>, about an epic blood feud, and <i><a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%A6nlendinga_saga" class="mw-redirect" title="Gr\xc3\xa6nlendinga saga">Gr\xc3\xa6nlendinga saga</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Saga_of_Erik_the_Red" title="Saga of Erik the Red">Eir\xc3\xadks saga</a></i>, describing the discovery and settlement of Greenland and Vinland (modern <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland</a>). <i><a href="/wiki/Egils_saga" class="mw-redirect" title="Egils saga">Egils saga</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Laxd%C3%A6la_saga" title="Laxd\xc3\xa6la saga">Laxd\xc3\xa6la saga</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Grettis_saga" title="Grettis saga">Grettis saga</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/G%C3%ADsla_saga" title="G\xc3\xadsla saga">G\xc3\xadsla saga</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Gunnlaugs_saga_ormstungu" title="Gunnlaugs saga ormstungu">Gunnlaugs saga ormstungu</a></i> are also notable and popular Icelanders\' sagas.\n</p><p>A translation of the Bible was published in the 16th century. Important compositions since the 15th to the 19th century include sacred verse, most famously the <a href="/wiki/Passion_Hymns" title="Passion Hymns">Passion Hymns</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hallgr%C3%ADmur_P%C3%A9tursson" title="Hallgr\xc3\xadmur P\xc3\xa9tursson">Hallgr\xc3\xadmur P\xc3\xa9tursson</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADmur" title="R\xc3\xadmur">r\xc3\xadmur</a></i>, rhyming epic poems. Originating in the 14th century, <i>r\xc3\xadmur</i> were popular into the 19th century, when the development of new literary forms was provoked by the influential, <a href="/wiki/Romantic_nationalism" title="Romantic nationalism">National-Romantic</a> writer <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3nas_Hallgr%C3%ADmsson" title="J\xc3\xb3nas Hallgr\xc3\xadmsson">J\xc3\xb3nas Hallgr\xc3\xadmsson</a>. In recent times, Iceland has produced many great writers, the best-known of whom is arguably <a href="/wiki/Halld%C3%B3r_Laxness" title="Halld\xc3\xb3r Laxness">Halld\xc3\xb3r Laxness</a>, who received the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> in 1955 (the only Icelander to win a Nobel Prize thus far). <a href="/wiki/Steinn_Steinarr" title="Steinn Steinarr">Steinn Steinarr</a> was an influential modernist poet during the early 20th century who remains popular.\n</p><p>Icelanders are avid consumers of literature, with the highest number of bookstores per capita in the world. For its size, Iceland imports and translates more international literature than any other nation.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated60_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated60-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> Iceland also has the highest per capita publication of books and magazines,<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> and around 10% of the population will publish a book in their lifetimes.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most books in Iceland are sold between late September to early November. This time period is known as <i>Jolabokaflod</i>, the Christmas Book Flood.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_222-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> The Flood begins with the Iceland Publisher\'s Association distributing <i>Bokatidindi</i>, a catalog of all new publications, free to each Icelandic home.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_222-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_art" title="Icelandic art">Icelandic art</a></div>\n<p>The distinctive rendition of the Icelandic landscape by its painters can be linked to nationalism and the movement for <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iceland#Home_rule_and_sovereignty" title="History of Iceland">home rule and independence</a>, which was very active in the mid-19th century.\n</p><p>Contemporary Icelandic painting is typically traced to the work of <a href="/wiki/%C3%9E%C3%B3rarinn_%C3%9Eorl%C3%A1ksson" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc3\x9e\xc3\xb3rarinn \xc3\x9eorl\xc3\xa1ksson">\xc3\x9e\xc3\xb3rarinn \xc3\x9eorl\xc3\xa1ksson</a>, who, following formal training in art in the 1890s in <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, returned to Iceland to paint and exhibit works from 1900 to his death in 1924, almost exclusively portraying the Icelandic landscape. Several other Icelandic men and women artists studied at <a href="/wiki/Royal_Danish_Academy_of_Fine_Arts" title="Royal Danish Academy of Fine Arts">Royal Danish Academy of Fine Arts</a> at that time, including <a href="/wiki/%C3%81sgr%C3%ADmur_J%C3%B3nsson" title="\xc3\x81sgr\xc3\xadmur J\xc3\xb3nsson">\xc3\x81sgr\xc3\xadmur J\xc3\xb3nsson</a>, who together with \xc3\x9e\xc3\xb3rarinn created a distinctive portrayal of Iceland\'s landscape in a romantic naturalistic style. Other landscape artists quickly followed in the footsteps of \xc3\x9e\xc3\xb3rarinn and \xc3\x81sgr\xc3\xadmur. These included <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3hannes_Sveinsson_Kjarval" title="J\xc3\xb3hannes Sveinsson Kjarval">J\xc3\xb3hannes Kjarval</a> and <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BAl%C3%ADana_Sveinsd%C3%B3ttir" title="J\xc3\xbal\xc3\xadana Sveinsd\xc3\xb3ttir">J\xc3\xbal\xc3\xadana Sveinsd\xc3\xb3ttir</a>. Kjarval in particular is noted for the distinct techniques in the application of paint that he developed in a concerted effort to render the characteristic <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_rock" title="Volcanic rock">volcanic rock</a> that dominates the Icelandic environment. <a href="/wiki/Einar_H%C3%A1konarson" title="Einar H\xc3\xa1konarson">Einar H\xc3\xa1konarson</a> is an expressionistic and figurative painter who by some is considered to have brought the figure back into Icelandic painting. In the 1980s, many Icelandic artists worked with the subject of the new painting in their work.\n</p><p>In the recent years artistic practice has multiplied, and the Icelandic art scene has become a setting for many large scale projects and exhibitions. The artist run gallery space Kling og Bang, members of which later ran the studio complex and exhibition venue Klink og Bank, has been a significant part of the trend of self-organised spaces, exhibitions and projects.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Living_Art_Museum" title="The Living Art Museum">The Living Art Museum</a>, Reykjav\xc3\xadk Municipal Art Museum, <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk_Art_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Reykjav\xc3\xadk Art Museum">Reykjav\xc3\xadk Art Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_of_Iceland" title="National Gallery of Iceland">National Gallery of Iceland</a> are the larger, more established institutions, curating shows and festivals.\n</p>\n<center>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 177.33333333333px"><div style="width: 177.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" class="gallerytext">\n<p>Traditional <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_turf_house" title="Icelandic turf house">Icelandic turf houses</a>. Until the 20th century, the vast majority of Icelanders lived in rural areas\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 223.33333333333px"><div style="width: 223.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 221.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Akureyri_Menntaskoli.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Akureyri_Menntaskoli.jpg/332px-Akureyri_Menntaskoli.jpg" width="222" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Akureyri_Menntaskoli.jpg/498px-Akureyri_Menntaskoli.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Akureyri_Menntaskoli.jpg/664px-Akureyri_Menntaskoli.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4436" data-file-height="2408" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>The old building (Gamli Sk\xc3\xb3li) of the Menntask\xc3\xb3li, i.e. High School precinct in Akureyri\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n</center>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Iceland" title="Music of Iceland">Music of Iceland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bj%C3%B6rk_-_Hurricane_Festival.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Bj%C3%B6rk_-_Hurricane_Festival.jpg/220px-Bj%C3%B6rk_-_Hurricane_Festival.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Bj%C3%B6rk_-_Hurricane_Festival.jpg/330px-Bj%C3%B6rk_-_Hurricane_Festival.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Bj%C3%B6rk_-_Hurricane_Festival.jpg/440px-Bj%C3%B6rk_-_Hurricane_Festival.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="756" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bj%C3%B6rk_-_Hurricane_Festival.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rk" title="Bj\xc3\xb6rk">Bj\xc3\xb6rk</a>, the best-known Icelandic musician</div></div></div>\n<p>Much Icelandic music is related to <a href="/wiki/Nordic_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Nordic music">Nordic music</a>, and includes <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> traditions. Notable Icelandic music acts include medieval music group <a href="/wiki/Voces_Thules" title="Voces Thules">Voces Thules</a>, alternative and indie rock acts such as <a href="/wiki/The_Sugarcubes" title="The Sugarcubes">The Sugarcubes</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B3ley" title="S\xc3\xb3ley">S\xc3\xb3ley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Of_Monsters_and_Men" title="Of Monsters and Men">Of Monsters and Men</a>, jazz fusion band <a href="/wiki/Mezzoforte_(band)" title="Mezzoforte (band)">Mezzoforte</a>, pop singers such as <a href="/wiki/Hafd%C3%ADs_Huld" title="Hafd\xc3\xads Huld">Hafd\xc3\xads Huld</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emil%C3%ADana_Torrini" title="Emil\xc3\xadana Torrini">Emil\xc3\xadana Torrini</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rk" title="Bj\xc3\xb6rk">Bj\xc3\xb6rk</a>, solo ballad singers like <a href="/wiki/Bubbi_Morthens" title="Bubbi Morthens">Bubbi Morthens</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Post-rock" title="Post-rock">post-rock</a> bands such as <a href="/wiki/Amiina" title="Amiina">Amiina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sigur_R%C3%B3s" title="Sigur R\xc3\xb3s">Sigur R\xc3\xb3s</a>. <a href="/wiki/Independent_music" title="Independent music">Independent music</a> is strong in Iceland, with bands such as <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BAm" title="M\xc3\xbam">m\xc3\xbam</a> and solo artists.\n</p><p>Traditional Icelandic music is strongly religious. Hymns, both religious and secular, are a particularly well-developed form of music, due to the scarcity of musical instruments throughout much of Iceland\'s history. Hallgr\xc3\xadmur P\xc3\xa9tursson wrote many Protestant hymns in the 17th century. Icelandic music was modernised in the 19th century, when Magn\xc3\xbas Stephensen brought pipe organs, which were followed by <a href="/wiki/Pump_organ" title="Pump organ">harmoniums</a>. Other vital traditions of Icelandic music are epic alliterative and rhyming ballads called r\xc3\xadmur. R\xc3\xadmur are epic tales, usually <a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a>, which can be traced back to <a href="/wiki/Skald" title="Skald">skaldic</a> poetry, using complex metaphors and elaborate rhyme schemes.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> The best known r\xc3\xadmur poet of the 19th century was <a href="/wiki/Sigur%C3%B0ur_Brei%C3%B0fj%C3%B6r%C3%B0" title="Sigur\xc3\xb0ur Brei\xc3\xb0fj\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb0">Sigur\xc3\xb0ur Brei\xc3\xb0fj\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb0</a> (1798\xe2\x80\x931846). A modern revitalisation of the tradition began in 1929 with the formation of I\xc3\xb0unn.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="What is I\xc3\xb0unn? Since it began in 1929, it must be something different from the goddess I\xc3\xb0unn. (October 2012)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Among Iceland\'s best-known classical composers are <a href="/wiki/Dan%C3%ADel_Bjarnason" title="Dan\xc3\xadel Bjarnason">Dan\xc3\xadel Bjarnason</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anna_S._%C3%9Eorvaldsd%C3%B3ttir" title="Anna S. \xc3\x9eorvaldsd\xc3\xb3ttir">Anna S. \xc3\x9eorvaldsd\xc3\xb3ttir</a> (Anna Thorvaldsdottir), who in 2012 received the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Council_Music_Prize" title="Nordic Council Music Prize">Nordic Council Music Prize</a> and in 2015 was chosen as the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Philharmonic" title="New York Philharmonic">New York Philharmonic</a>\'s Kravis Emerging Composer, an honor that includes a $50,000 cash prize and a commission to write a composition for the orchestra; she is the second recipient.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_anthem" title="National anthem">national anthem</a> of Iceland is <i><a href="/wiki/Lofs%C3%B6ngur" title="Lofs\xc3\xb6ngur">Lofs\xc3\xb6ngur</a></i>, written by <a href="/wiki/Matth%C3%ADas_Jochumsson" title="Matth\xc3\xadas Jochumsson">Matth\xc3\xadas Jochumsson</a>, with music by <a href="/wiki/Sveinbj%C3%B6rn_Sveinbj%C3%B6rnsson" title="Sveinbj\xc3\xb6rn Sveinbj\xc3\xb6rnsson">Sveinbj\xc3\xb6rn Sveinbj\xc3\xb6rnsson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltasar_Kormakur.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Baltasar_Kormakur.jpg/220px-Baltasar_Kormakur.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Baltasar_Kormakur.jpg/330px-Baltasar_Kormakur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Baltasar_Kormakur.jpg/440px-Baltasar_Kormakur.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltasar_Kormakur.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Icelandic director <a href="/wiki/Baltasar_Korm%C3%A1kur" title="Baltasar Korm\xc3\xa1kur">Baltasar Korm\xc3\xa1kur</a>, best known for the films <i><a href="/wiki/101_Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="101 Reykjav\xc3\xadk">101 Reykjav\xc3\xadk</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Jar_City_(film)" title="Jar City (film)">Jar City</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Contraband_(2012_film)" title="Contraband (2012 film)"><i>Contraband</i></a>, and television series <i><a href="/wiki/Trapped_(Icelandic_TV_series)" title="Trapped (Icelandic TV series)">Trapped</a></i></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Iceland" title="Media of Iceland">Media of Iceland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Iceland" title="Cinema of Iceland">Cinema of Iceland</a></div>\n<p>Iceland\'s largest television stations are the state-run <a href="/wiki/Sj%C3%B3nvarpi%C3%B0" class="mw-redirect" title="Sj\xc3\xb3nvarpi\xc3\xb0">Sj\xc3\xb3nvarpi\xc3\xb0</a> and the privately owned <a href="/wiki/St%C3%B6%C3%B0_2" title="St\xc3\xb6\xc3\xb0 2">St\xc3\xb6\xc3\xb0 2</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skj%C3%A1rEinn" class="mw-redirect" title="Skj\xc3\xa1rEinn">Skj\xc3\xa1rEinn</a>. Smaller stations exist, many of them local. Radio is broadcast throughout the country, including some parts of the interior. The main radio stations are <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A1s_1" title="R\xc3\xa1s 1">R\xc3\xa1s 1</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A1s_2" title="R\xc3\xa1s 2">R\xc3\xa1s 2</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=X-i%C3%B0_977&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="X-i\xc3\xb0 977 (page does not exist)">X-i\xc3\xb0 977</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bylgjan" title="Bylgjan">Bylgjan</a> and <a href="/wiki/FM_957_(Icelandic_Radio_Station)" title="FM 957 (Icelandic Radio Station)">FM957</a>. The daily newspapers are <a href="/wiki/Morgunbla%C3%B0i%C3%B0" title="Morgunbla\xc3\xb0i\xc3\xb0">Morgunbla\xc3\xb0i\xc3\xb0</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9ttabla%C3%B0i%C3%B0" title="Fr\xc3\xa9ttabla\xc3\xb0i\xc3\xb0">Fr\xc3\xa9ttabla\xc3\xb0i\xc3\xb0</a>. The most popular websites are the news sites <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADsir" title="V\xc3\xadsir">V\xc3\xadsir</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mbl.is" class="mw-redirect" title="Mbl.is">Mbl.is</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Iceland is home to <i><a href="/wiki/LazyTown" title="LazyTown">LazyTown</a></i> (Icelandic: <i>Latib\xc3\xa6r</i>), a children\'s educational musical comedy program created by <a href="/wiki/Magn%C3%BAs_Scheving" title="Magn\xc3\xbas Scheving">Magn\xc3\xbas Scheving</a>. It has become a very popular programme for children and adults and is shown in over 100 countries, including the Americas, the UK and Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> The <i>LazyTown</i> studios are located in <a href="/wiki/Gar%C3%B0ab%C3%A6r" title="Gar\xc3\xb0ab\xc3\xa6r">Gar\xc3\xb0ab\xc3\xa6r</a>. The 2015 television crime series <i><a href="/wiki/Trapped_(Icelandic_TV_series)" title="Trapped (Icelandic TV series)">Trapped</a></i> aired in the UK on BBC4 in February and March 2016, to critical acclaim and according to the Guardian "the unlikeliest TV hit of the year".<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1992, the Icelandic film industry achieved its greatest recognition hitherto, when <a href="/wiki/Fri%C3%B0rik_%C3%9E%C3%B3r_Fri%C3%B0riksson" title="Fri\xc3\xb0rik \xc3\x9e\xc3\xb3r Fri\xc3\xb0riksson">Fri\xc3\xb0rik \xc3\x9e\xc3\xb3r Fri\xc3\xb0riksson</a> was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Foreign_Language_Film" title="Academy Award for Best Foreign Language Film">Academy Award for Best Foreign Language Film</a> for his <i><a href="/wiki/Children_of_Nature" title="Children of Nature">Children of Nature</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> It features the story of an old man who is unable to continue running his farm. After being unwelcomed in his daughter\'s and father-in-law\'s house in town, he is put in a home for the elderly. There, he meets an old girlfriend of his youth and they both begin a journey through the wilds of Iceland to die together. This is the only Icelandic movie to have ever been nominated for an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Oscars1992_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oscars1992-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rk" title="Bj\xc3\xb6rk">Bj\xc3\xb6rk</a> received international acclaim for her starring role in the Danish musical drama <i><a href="/wiki/Dancer_in_the_Dark" title="Dancer in the Dark">Dancer in the Dark</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Lars_von_Trier" title="Lars von Trier">Lars von Trier</a>, in which she plays Selma Je\xc5\xbekov\xc3\xa1, a factory worker who struggles to pay for her son\'s eye operation. The film premiered at the <a href="/wiki/2000_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="2000 Cannes Film Festival">2000 Cannes Film Festival</a>, where she won the Best Actress Award. The movie also led Bj\xc3\xb6rk to nominations for <a href="/wiki/Best_Original_Song" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Original Song">Best Original Song</a> at the <a href="/wiki/73rd_Academy_Awards" title="73rd Academy Awards">73rd Academy Awards</a>, with the song <i><a href="/wiki/I%27ve_Seen_It_All" title="I&#39;ve Seen It All">I\'ve Seen It All</a></i> and for a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Motion_Picture_-_Drama" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress in a Motion Picture - Drama">Golden Globe Award for Best Actress in a Motion Picture - Drama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gu\xc3\xb0r\xc3\xban S. G\xc3\xadslad\xc3\xb3ttir, who is Icelandic, played one of the major roles in Russian filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Tarkovsky" title="Andrei Tarkovsky">Andrei Tarkovsky</a>\'s 1986 film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sacrifice" title="The Sacrifice">The Sacrifice</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Anita_Briem" title="Anita Briem">Anita Briem</a>, known for her performance in <a href="/wiki/Showtime_(TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Showtime (TV channel)">Showtime</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tudors" title="The Tudors">The Tudors</a></i>, is also Icelandic. Briem starred in the 2008 film <i><a href="/wiki/Journey_to_the_Center_of_the_Earth_(2008_Hollywood_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Journey to the Center of the Earth (2008 Hollywood film)">Journey to the Center of the Earth</a></i>, which shot scenes in Iceland. The 2002 <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a> movie <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Another_Day" title="Die Another Day">Die Another Day</a></i> is set for a large-part in Iceland. <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Nolan" title="Christopher Nolan">Christopher Nolan</a>\'s 2014 film, <i><a href="/wiki/Interstellar_(film)" title="Interstellar (film)">Interstellar</a></i> was also filmed in Iceland for some of its scenes, as was <a href="/wiki/Ridley_Scott" title="Ridley Scott">Ridley Scott</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Prometheus_(2012_film)" title="Prometheus (2012 film)">Prometheus</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 17 June 2010, the parliament passed the <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_Modern_Media_Initiative" title="Icelandic Modern Media Initiative">Icelandic Modern Media Initiative</a>, proposing greater protection of free speech rights and the identity of journalists and whistle-blowers\xe2\x80\x94the strongest journalist protection law in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> According to a 2011 report by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>, Iceland is one of the highest ranked countries in press freedom.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/CCP_Games" title="CCP Games">CCP Games</a>, developers of the critically acclaimed EVE Online and Dust 514, is headquartered in Reykjav\xc3\xadk. CCP Games hosts the third most populated <a href="/wiki/Massively_multiplayer_online_game" title="Massively multiplayer online game">MMO</a> in the world, which also has the largest total game area for an online game.\n</p><p>Iceland has a highly developed <a href="/wiki/Cyberculture" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyberculture">internet culture</a>, with around 95% of the population having internet access, the highest proportion in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> Iceland ranked 12th in the World Economic Forum\'s 2009\xe2\x80\x932010 <a href="/wiki/Network_Readiness_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Network Readiness Index">Network Readiness Index</a>, which measures a country\'s ability to competitively exploit communications technology.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunication_Union" title="International Telecommunication Union">United Nations International Telecommunication Union</a> ranks the country 3rd in its development of information and communications technology, having moved up four places between 2008 and 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> In February 2013 the country (ministry of the interior) was researching possible methods to protect children in regards to Internet pornography, claiming that pornography online is a threat to children as it supports child slavery and abuse. Strong voices within the community expressed concerns with this, stating that it is impossible to block access to pornography without compromising freedom of speech.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_cuisine" title="Icelandic cuisine">Icelandic cuisine</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Eorramatur" title="\xc3\x9eorramatur">\xc3\x9eorramatur</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thorramatur.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Thorramatur.jpg/220px-Thorramatur.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Thorramatur.jpg/330px-Thorramatur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Thorramatur.jpg/440px-Thorramatur.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thorramatur.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A typical <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Eorramatur" title="\xc3\x9eorramatur">\xc3\x9eorramatur</a> assortment</div></div></div>\n<p>Much of Iceland\'s cuisine is based on fish, <a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">lamb</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dairy_product" title="Dairy product">dairy products</a>, with little to no utilization of herbs or spices. Due to the island\'s climate, fruits and vegetables are not generally a component of traditional dishes, although the use of greenhouses has made them more common in contemporary food. <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Eorramatur" title="\xc3\x9eorramatur">\xc3\x9eorramatur</a> is a selection of traditional cuisine consisting of many dishes, and is usually consumed around the month of <a href="/wiki/Month#Germanic_calendar" title="Month">\xc3\x9eorri</a>, which begins on the first Friday after 19 January. Traditional dishes also include <a href="/wiki/Skyr" title="Skyr">skyr</a> (a yoghurt-like cheese), <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A1karl" title="H\xc3\xa1karl">h\xc3\xa1karl</a> (cured shark), cured ram, singed sheep heads, and <a href="/wiki/Black_pudding" title="Black pudding">black pudding</a>, Flatkaka (flat bread), dried fish and dark rye bread traditionally baked in the ground in geothermal areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Icelandic_delicacies_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Icelandic_delicacies-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Puffin" title="Puffin">Puffin</a> is considered a local delicacy that is often prepared through broiling.\n</p><p>Breakfast usually consists of pancakes, cereal, fruit, and coffee, while lunch may take the form of a <a href="/wiki/Sm%C3%B6rg%C3%A5sbord" title="Sm\xc3\xb6rg\xc3\xa5sbord">sm\xc3\xb6rg\xc3\xa5sbord</a>. The main meal of the day for most Icelanders is dinner, which usually involves fish or lamb as the main course. Seafood is central to most Icelandic cooking, particularly <a href="/wiki/Cod" title="Cod">cod</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haddock" title="Haddock">haddock</a> but also <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">salmon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herring" title="Herring">herring</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Halibut" title="Halibut">halibut</a>. It is often prepared in a wide variety of ways, either smoked, pickled, boiled, or dried. Lamb is by far the most common meat, and it tends to be either smoke-cured (known as <i><a href="/wiki/Hangikj%C3%B6t" title="Hangikj\xc3\xb6t">hangikj\xc3\xb6t</a></i>) or salt-preserved (<i>saltkj\xc3\xb6t</i>). Many older dishes make use of every part of the sheep, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Sl%C3%A1tur" title="Sl\xc3\xa1tur">sl\xc3\xa1tur</a></i>, which consists of <a href="/wiki/Offal" title="Offal">offal</a> (internal organs and entrails) minced together with blood and served in sheep stomach. Additionally, boiled or mashed potatoes, pickled cabbage, green beans, and rye bread are prevalent side dishes.\n</p><p>Coffee is a popular beverage in Iceland, with the country being third placed by per capita consumption worldwide in 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> and is drunk at breakfast, after meals, and with a light snack in mid-afternoon. <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> is also widely consumed, to the extent that the country is said to have one of the highest per capita consumption rates in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Iceland\'s signature alcoholic beverage is <i><a href="/wiki/Brenniv%C3%ADn" title="Brenniv\xc3\xadn">brenniv\xc3\xadn</a></i> (literally "burnt [i.e., distilled] wine"), which is similar in flavouring to the <a href="/wiki/Akvavit" title="Akvavit">akvavit</a> variant of Scandinavian <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%A4nnvin" title="Br\xc3\xa4nnvin">br\xc3\xa4nnvin</a>. It is a type of <a href="/wiki/Schnapps" title="Schnapps">schnapps</a> made from distilled potatoes and flavoured with either <a href="/wiki/Caraway" title="Caraway">caraway</a> seeds or <a href="/wiki/Angelica" title="Angelica">angelica</a>. Its potency has earned it the nickname <i>svarti dau\xc3\xb0i</i> ("Black Death"). Modern distilleries on Iceland produce <a href="/wiki/Vodka" title="Vodka">vodka</a> (<a href="/wiki/Reyka" title="Reyka">Reyka</a>), <a href="/wiki/Gin" title="Gin">gin</a> (\xc3\x8dsafold), <a href="/wiki/Moss" title="Moss">moss</a> schnapps (Fjallagrasa), and a <a href="/wiki/Birch" title="Birch">birch</a>-flavoured schnapps and <a href="/wiki/Liqueur" title="Liqueur">liqueur</a> (Foss Distillery\xe2\x80\x99s Birkir and Bj\xc3\xb6rk). Martin Miller blends Icelandic water with its England-distilled gin on the island. Strong beer was <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_Iceland" title="Prohibition in Iceland">banned until 1989</a>, so <i>bj\xc3\xb3rl\xc3\xadki</i>, a mixture of legal, low-alcohol <a href="/wiki/Pilsner" title="Pilsner">pilsner</a> beer and vodka, became popular. Several strong beers are now made by Icelandic breweries.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Iceland" title="Sport in Iceland">Sport in Iceland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Iceland%27s_Olympic_Handball_Team,_Beijing_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Iceland%27s_Olympic_Handball_Team%2C_Beijing_2008.jpg/220px-Iceland%27s_Olympic_Handball_Team%2C_Beijing_2008.jpg" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Iceland%27s_Olympic_Handball_Team%2C_Beijing_2008.jpg/330px-Iceland%27s_Olympic_Handball_Team%2C_Beijing_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Iceland%27s_Olympic_Handball_Team%2C_Beijing_2008.jpg/440px-Iceland%27s_Olympic_Handball_Team%2C_Beijing_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2203" data-file-height="1261" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iceland%27s_Olympic_Handball_Team,_Beijing_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Iceland_national_handball_team" title="Iceland national handball team">Iceland national handball team</a> (pictured) <a href="/wiki/Handball_at_the_2008_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Handball at the 2008 Summer Olympics \xe2\x80\x93 Men&#39;s tournament">won the silver medal</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a>. <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">Handball</a> is considered Iceland\'s national sport.<sup id="cite_ref-handball_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-handball-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Sport is an important part of Icelandic culture, as the population is generally quite active.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> The main traditional sport in Iceland is <i><a href="/wiki/Gl%C3%ADma" class="mw-redirect" title="Gl\xc3\xadma">Gl\xc3\xadma</a></i>, a form of <a href="/wiki/Wrestling" title="Wrestling">wrestling</a> thought to have originated in medieval times.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FWC_2018_-_Group_D_-_ARG_v_ISL_-_Photo_195.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/FWC_2018_-_Group_D_-_ARG_v_ISL_-_Photo_195.jpg/220px-FWC_2018_-_Group_D_-_ARG_v_ISL_-_Photo_195.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/FWC_2018_-_Group_D_-_ARG_v_ISL_-_Photo_195.jpg/330px-FWC_2018_-_Group_D_-_ARG_v_ISL_-_Photo_195.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/FWC_2018_-_Group_D_-_ARG_v_ISL_-_Photo_195.jpg/440px-FWC_2018_-_Group_D_-_ARG_v_ISL_-_Photo_195.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FWC_2018_-_Group_D_-_ARG_v_ISL_-_Photo_195.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Iceland fans at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a> in Russia</div></div></div><p>Popular sports include <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a>, <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>. Handball is often referred to as the national sport.<sup id="cite_ref-handball_247-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-handball-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Iceland_national_football_team" title="Iceland national football team">Icelandic national football team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">2016</a> <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship" title="UEFA European Championship">UEFA European football championship</a> for the first time. They recorded a draw against later winners <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese national football team">Portugal</a> in the group stage, and defeated <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> 2\xe2\x80\x931 in the round of 16, with goals from <a href="/wiki/Ragnar_Sigur%C3%B0sson" title="Ragnar Sigur\xc3\xb0sson">Ragnar Sigur\xc3\xb0sson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kolbeinn_Sig%C3%BE%C3%B3rsson" title="Kolbeinn Sig\xc3\xbe\xc3\xb3rsson">Kolbeinn Sig\xc3\xbe\xc3\xb3rsson</a>. They then lost to hosts and later finalists <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a> in the quarter finals.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_2017-08-03_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_2017-08-03-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> Following up on this, Iceland made its debut at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018</a> <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a>. For both the European and the world championship, Iceland is to date the smallest nation in terms of population to qualify.\n</p><p>Iceland has excellent conditions for <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snowboarding" title="Snowboarding">snowboarding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ice_climbing" title="Ice climbing">ice climbing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rock_climbing" title="Rock climbing">rock climbing</a>, although <a href="/wiki/Mountain_climbing" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain climbing">mountain climbing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">hiking</a> are preferred by the general public. Iceland is also a world-class destination for alpine ski touring and <a href="/wiki/Telemark_skiing" title="Telemark skiing">Telemark skiing</a>, with the Troll Peninsula in Northern Iceland being the main centre of activity. Although the country\'s environment is generally ill-suited for golf, there are nevertheless lots of golf courses throughout the island, and Iceland has a greater percentage of the population playing golf than Scotland with over 17,000 registered golfers out of a population of approximately 300,000.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> Iceland hosts an annual international golf tournament known as the Arctic Open played through the night during the summer solstice at <a href="/wiki/Akureyri_Golf_Club" title="Akureyri Golf Club">Akureyri Golf Club</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-w111_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w111-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> Iceland has also won the second most <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Strongest_Man" title="World&#39;s Strongest Man">World\'s Strongest Man</a> competitions of any country with nine titles, including four by both <a href="/wiki/Magn%C3%BAs_Ver_Magn%C3%BAsson" title="Magn\xc3\xbas Ver Magn\xc3\xbasson">Magn\xc3\xbas Ver Magn\xc3\xbasson</a> and <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3n_P%C3%A1ll_Sigmarsson" title="J\xc3\xb3n P\xc3\xa1ll Sigmarsson">J\xc3\xb3n P\xc3\xa1ll Sigmarsson</a> and most recently <a href="/wiki/Haf%C3%BE%C3%B3r_J%C3%BAl%C3%ADus_Bj%C3%B6rnsson" title="Haf\xc3\xbe\xc3\xb3r J\xc3\xbal\xc3\xadus Bj\xc3\xb6rnsson">Haf\xc3\xbe\xc3\xb3r J\xc3\xbal\xc3\xadus Bj\xc3\xb6rnsson</a> in 2018.\n</p><p>Iceland is also one of the leading countries in <a href="/wiki/Ocean_rowing" title="Ocean rowing">ocean rowing</a>, Icelandic rower <a href="/wiki/Fiann_Paul" title="Fiann Paul">Fiann Paul</a> became the fastest and the most record-breaking ocean rower. He has claimed overall speed <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a> for the fastest rowing of all four oceans (Atlantic, Indian, Pacific and Arctic) in a <a href="/wiki/Human-powered_watercraft" title="Human-powered watercraft">man-powered row boat</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness</a> title of the first rower to ever hold the record for all four oceans simultaneously, claiming 24 Guinness  World Records in total for Iceland by 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Swimming is popular in Iceland. Geothermally heated outdoor pools are widespread, and swimming courses are a mandatory part of the national curriculum.<sup id="cite_ref-w111_252-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w111-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Horseback_riding" class="mw-redirect" title="Horseback riding">Horseback riding</a>, which was historically the most prevalent form of transportation on the island, remains a common pursuit for many Icelanders.\n</p><p>The oldest sport association in Iceland is the Reykjav\xc3\xadk Shooting Association, founded in 1867. Rifle shooting became very popular in the 19th century with the encouragement of politicians and nationalists who were pushing for Icelandic independence. To this day, it remains a significant pastime.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Iceland has also produced many chess masters and hosted the historic <a href="/wiki/World_Chess_Championship_1972" title="World Chess Championship 1972">World Chess Championship 1972</a> in Reykjav\xc3\xadk during the height of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. As of  2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there have been nine Icelandic chess grandmasters, a considerable number given the small size of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bridge_(card_game)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bridge (card game)">Bridge</a> is also popular, with Iceland participating in a number of international tournaments. Iceland won the world bridge championship (the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Bowl" title="Bermuda Bowl">Bermuda Bowl</a>) in Yokohama, Japan, in 1991 and took second place (with Sweden) in Hamilton, Bermuda, in 1950.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iceland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation"
